TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
OFFICIAL CITY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Adoption Of Code
1-1-2: Title; Citation; Reference
1-1-3: Contents
1-1-4: Application To Amendments
1-1-5: Title, Chapter And Section Headings
1-1-6: Reference To Specific Ordinances
1-1-7: Code Alterations
1-1-1: ADOPTION OF CODE:
There is adopted the Clatskanie municipal code as published by Sterling
Codifiers, Inc., Coeur d'Alene, Idaho. (1996 Code § 1.01.010; amd. 2004 Code)
1-1-2: TITLE; CITATION; REFERENCE:
This code shall be known as the CLATSKANIE MUNICIPAL CODE and it shall be
sufficient to refer to the code as the "Clatskanie municipal code" in any
prosecution for the violation of any provision thereof or in any proceeding at
law or equity. It shall be sufficient to designate any ordinance adding to,
amending, correcting or repealing all or any part or portion thereof as an
addition to, amendment to, correction or repeal of the "Clatskanie municipal
code". Further reference may be had to the titles, chapters, sections and
subsections of the "Clatskanie municipal code", and such references shall apply
to that numbered title, chapter, section or subsection as it appears in this
code. (1996 Code § 1.01.020; amd. 2004 Code)
1-1-3: CONTENTS:
This code consists of the regulatory and penal ordinances and certain of the
administrative ordinances of the city. (1996 Code § 1.01.030)
1-1-4: APPLICATION TO AMENDMENTS:
Whenever a reference is made to this code as the "Clatskanie municipal code" or
to any portion thereof, or to any ordinance of the city, the reference shall
apply to all amendments, corrections and additions made before, as of or after
the effective date hereof. (1996 Code § 1.01.050)
1-1-5: TITLE, CHAPTER AND SECTION HEADINGS:
Title, chapter and section headings contained in this code shall not be deemed
to govern, limit, modify or in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent
of the provisions of any title, chapter or section of this code. (1996 Code §
1.01.060)
1-1-6: REFERENCE TO SPECIFIC ORDINANCES:
The provisions of this code shall not in any manner affect matters of record
which refer to, or are otherwise connected with, ordinances which are therein
specifically designated by number or otherwise and which are included within
the code, but such reference shall be construed to apply to the corresponding
provisions contained within this code. (1996 Code § 1.01.070)
1-1-7: CODE ALTERATIONS:
It shall be deemed unlawful for any person to alter, change, replace or deface
in any way any section or any page of this city code in such a manner that the
meaning of any phrase or order may be changed or omitted. Said code, while in
actual possession of officials and other interested persons, shall be and
remain the property of the city and shall be returned to the office of the city
recorder when directed so to do by order of the city council. (2004 Code)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Public Ways And Public Utility Ordinances
1-2-3: Court Proceedings
1-2-4: Severability Clause
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
All general ordinances of the city passed prior to the adoption of this city
code are hereby repealed, except such as are included in this city code or are
by necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to the saving
clauses contained in the following sections), and excluding the following
ordinances which are not hereby repealed: tax levy ordinances; appropriation
ordinances; ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations; franchise
ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to persons or
corporations; contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants; salary ordinances; ordinances
establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other public places;
improvement ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances relating to elections;
ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the
city; and all special ordinances. (2004 Code)
1-2-2: PUBLIC WAYS AND PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroad crossings with streets and other public ways,
or relating to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public utilities shall
be repealed by virtue of the adoption of this city code or by virtue of the
preceding section, excepting as the city code may contain provisions for such
matters, in which case, this city code shall be considered as amending such
ordinance or ordinances in respect to such provisions only. (2004 Code)
1-2-3: COURT PROCEEDINGS:
   A.   Prior Acts: No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a
former ordinance whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as
to any offense committed against such former ordinance or as to any act done,
any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued or
claim arising under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect any
such offense or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or
punishment so incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new
ordinance takes effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform
to the ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding, so far as
practicable. If any penalty, forfeiture or punishment may be mitigated by any
provision of a new ordinance, such provision may be, by consent of the party
affected, applied to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes
effect.
   B.   Extend To All Repeals: This section shall extend to all repeals, either
by express words or implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making
any new provisions upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
   C.   Current Pending Actions: Nothing contained in this chapter shall be
construed as abating any action now pending under or by virtue of any general
ordinance of the city herein repealed, and the provisions of all general
ordinances contained in this code shall be deemed to be continuing provisions
and not a new enactment of the same provisions; nor shall this chapter be
deemed as discontinuing, abating, modifying or altering any penalty accrued or
to accrue, or as affecting the liability of any person, firm or corporation, or
as waiving any right of the city under any ordinance or provision thereof in
force at the time of the adoption of this city code. (2004 Code)
1-2-4: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
If any section, subsection, subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase
of this city code, or any part hereof or any portion adopted by reference or
any codes or portions of codes adopted herein is for any reason held to be
unconstitutional or invalid or ineffective by any court of competent
jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity or effectiveness of
the remaining portions of this code, or any part hereof or any portion adopted
by reference or any codes or portions of codes adopted herein. The city council
hereby declares that it would have passed each section, subsection,
subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase thereof irrespective of the
fact that any one or more sections, subsections, subdivisions, paragraphs,
sentences, clauses or phrases be declared unconstitutional, invalid or
ineffective. (2004 Code)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
1-3-1: Construction Of Words
1-3-2: Definitions, General
1-3-1: CONSTRUCTION OF WORDS:
   A.   Whenever any word in any section of this city code importing the plural
number is used in describing or referring to any matters, parties or persons,
any single matter, party or person shall be deemed to be included, although
distributive words may not have been used.
   B.   When any subject matter, party or person is referred to in this city
code by words importing the singular number only, or the masculine gender,
several matters, parties or persons and females as well as males and bodies
corporate shall be deemed to be included; provided, that these rules of
construction shall not be applied to any section of this city code which
contains any express provision excluding such construction or where the subject
matter or context may be repugnant thereto.
   C.   The word "ordinance" contained in the ordinances of the city has been
changed in the content of this city code to "title", "chapter", "section" and/
or "subsection" or words of like import for organizational and clarification
purposes only. Such change to the city's ordinances is not meant to amend
passage and effective dates of such original ordinances. (2004 Code)
1-3-2: DEFINITIONS, GENERAL:
Whenever the following words or terms are used in this code, they shall have
such meanings herein ascribed to them, unless the context makes such meaning
repugnant thereto:
AGENT: A person acting on behalf of another with authority conferred, either
expressly or by implication.
CHIEF OF POLICE: The appointed director of the police department.
CITY: The city of Clatskanie, county of Columbia, state of Oregon.
CODE: The municipal code of the city of Clatskanie.
COUNCIL: Unless otherwise indicated, the mayor and city council of the city of
Clatskanie.
COUNTY: The county of Columbia, state of Oregon.
EMPLOYEES: Whenever reference is made in this code to a city employee by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the city of
Clatskanie".
FEE: A sum of money charged by the city for the carrying on of a business,
profession or occupation.
LICENSE: The permission granted for the carrying on of a business, profession
or occupation.
OAR: Oregon administrative rules.
ORS: Oregon Revised Statutes.
OCCUPANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land whether alone or with
others.
OFFENSE: Any act forbidden by any provision of this code or the omission of any
act required by the provisions of this code.
OFFICERS: Whenever reference is made in this code to a city officer by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the city of
Clatskanie".
OPERATOR: The person who is in charge of any operation, business or profession.
OWNER: A person with the legal right of possession or lawful title to property,
either real or personal.
PERSON: Includes a natural person, joint venture, joint stock company,
partnership, association, club, company, corporation, business, trust,
organization, or the manager, lessee, agent, servant, officer or employee of
any of them.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Shall include every description of money, goods, chattels,
effects, evidence of rights in action and all written instruments by which any
pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created, acknowledged,
transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished and every right or
interest therein.
PUBLIC TRANSIT FACILITIES: Include one or more of the following: a bus stop,
building shelter, or park and ride lot where bus service is accessed.
RETAILER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to relate
to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things in small quantities
direct to the consumer.
RIGHT OF WAY: The privilege of the immediate use of the roadway or other
property.
STREET: Shall include alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public
squares, public places and sidewalks.
TENANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who occupies
the whole or any part of such building or land, whether alone or with others.
WHOLESALER, WHOLESALE DEALER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, these
terms shall be understood to relate to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles
or things in quantity to persons who purchase for the purpose of resale.
WRITTEN, IN WRITING: May include printing and any other mode of representing
words and letters, but when the written signature of any person is required by
law to any official or public writing or bond, it shall be in the proper
handwriting of such person, or in case he is unable to write, by his proper
mark. (1996 Code §§ 1.04.070, 1.04.320, 1.04.330; amd. 2004 Code; Ord. 658, 11-
4-2009)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY; ASSESSMENTS AND FEES
SECTION:
1-4-1: Penalty For Code Violations
1-4-2: Assessments And Fees Established
1-4-1: PENALTY FOR CODE VIOLATIONS:
Unless otherwise stated in this code, any violation of any ordinance of this
code shall be punishable by a fine not to exceed one hundred dollars ($100.00).
Each day's violation of any provision of this code constitutes a separate
offense. (2004 Code)
1-4-2: ASSESSMENTS AND FEES ESTABLISHED:
   A.   Schedule Of Fees: The schedule of municipal court assessments and fees
shall comprise the following:
      1.   State Mandated Assessments: Any assessment amounts mandated by state
law shall be collected according to the provisions of state law.
      2.   City Assessment: Court costs shall be separate and distinct from any
fine, assessment or other penalty imposed by the court, such assessments shall
be set by the city council.
   B.   General Fund: The city shall account for such assessment and fees as
appropriate to ensure legal compliance for the financial management of such
funds. Any such funds remaining unexpended at the end of each fiscal year will
remain in the general fund as undedicated revenue. (2004 Code)
CHAPTER 5
COUNCIL RULES
SECTION:
1-5-1: Authority
1-5-2: Mayor And Council
1-5-3: Council Meetings
1-5-4: Agenda And Order Of Business
1-5-5: Procedure For Council Meetings
1-5-6: Decorum And Order
1-5-7: Censure
1-5-8: Code Of Ethics
1-5-9: Council Relations With City Staff
1-5-10: Committees
1-5-11: Confidentiality
1-5-12: Suspension Or Amendment Of Rules
1-5-1: AUTHORITY:
   A.   City Charter: The charter of the city in chapter IV, section 14,
"Rules", specifies: "The council shall, by ordinance, prescribe rules to govern
its meetings and proceedings".
   B.   Effective Date: The rules adopted in this chapter shall be in effect
upon their adoption by the city council and until such time as they are
amended, added to, deleted or replaced in the manner provided by these rules.
   C.   Application: These rules apply equally to the mayor and councilors.
   D.   Compliance With Charter: These rules are to be observed in addition to
and may not be contradictory to the current city charter. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
1-5-2: MAYOR AND COUNCIL:
The mayor and council (hereafter, council) are the policy making body of the
city. The council speaks on policies and issues with one voice or not at all.
Council decisions may not be unanimous but once voted upon define the position
of the entire council. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
1-5-3: COUNCIL MEETINGS:
   A.   Regular Meetings: Regular meetings of the council will be held the
first Wednesday of each month at seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. in the council
chambers at Clatskanie city hall. (Ord. 642, 12-7-2005, eff. 1-1-2006)
   B.   Time And Date Of Meetings; Notice:
      1.   Time and date of the regular council meetings may be changed for
special circumstances, to facilitate work sessions or in order to have a quorum
of councilors at the meeting.
      2.   Regular meeting notice requirements must be followed.
   C.   Special Meetings: Special meetings of the council may be called at any
time on the request of three (3) members of the council, by the mayor, or by
the president of the council in the mayor's absence, by giving notice of the
meeting to the council members and the public at least twenty four (24) hours
in advance in a manner and for such time as the exigencies of the case may
permit, but with a view to obtaining the largest possible attendance of council
members.
   D.   Additional Or Alternate Meetings: Although the council may choose other
days in which to hold their meetings, the third Wednesday shall be the
preferred alternate meeting time.
   E.   Emergency Meetings: Emergency meetings of the council are considered
special meetings which can be called when no more than twenty four (24) hours'
notice can be given. The minutes need to state the nature of the emergency.
Emergency meetings may be held by consent of a majority of councilors. An
attempt must be made to notify the public or the press of the need for this
emergency meeting.
   F.   Workshop Or Training Meetings:
      1.   Workshop or training meetings of the council may be held at the
convenience of the council at a time when as many as possible can attend. These
meetings may be held for council goal setting, new councilor training, or
longer workshops for planning programs or projects.
      2.   Goal setting retreats may be held outside the city so long as no
decision making or discussion toward decisions occurs. Any goals arrived at by
any process should be confirmed in public at a regular council meeting.
      3.   The council may decide if the public is welcome at any of these
meetings and they may be held without opportunity for public input.
   G.   Executive Sessions:
      1.   Executive sessions may be held by the council pursuant to Oregon
Revised Statutes 192.640, 192.650, 192.660 and 192.670. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
      2.   Only those staff members required to attend will be present. (Ord.
600, 12-1-1999; amd. 2004 Code)
   H.   Public Meetings:
      1.   Public meetings of the council will be held in accordance with
Oregon Revised Statutes 192.610 through 192.710.
      2.   All regular and special meetings will be open to the public and
provide an opportunity for public input.
   I.   Attendance: Councilors should inform the mayor, city manager or city
recorder if unable to attend any council meeting. The mayor will inform the
council president if unable to attend any council meeting. (Ord. 600, 12-1-
1999)
1-5-4: AGENDA AND ORDER OF BUSINESS:
   A.   Preparation And Distribution Of Agenda: An agenda for each regular
council meeting shall be prepared by the city manager. The mayor or the city
council may direct that specific items be included on the agenda. The city
manager should be given enough time to do necessary research or prepare
necessary reports to address the agenda items. Agendas and informational
material should be distributed to the council at least four (4) days prior to
the meeting.
   B.   Order Of Business: The normal order of business for a regular council
meeting shall be as follows:
      1.   Call to order.
      2.   Flag salute.
      3.   Public input.
      4.   Consent agenda.
Minutes
Payment of bills
Liquor license permits
Bid awards
Resolutions
      5.   Presentations (prearranged).
      6.   Public hearings.
      7.   Action items.
      8.   Ordinances, first readings.
      9.   Ordinances, second readings and passage.
      10.   Manager's report.
      11.   Councilors' items.
      12.   Mayor's items.
      13.   Executive session.
      14.   Action as the result of the executive session (if required).
      15.   Adjournment.
   C.   Agenda Items Taken Out Of Order; Mayor's Discretion: The mayor may
consider agenda items out of order as he deems necessary to facilitate the
efficient management of the agenda. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
1-5-5: PROCEDURE FOR COUNCIL MEETINGS:
   A.   Rules Of Order: Unless otherwise provided by law or by these rules, the
procedure for council meetings shall be governed by "Robert's Rules Of Order".
The mayor, as presiding officer, may utilize "Robert's Rules Of Order" as
necessary.
   B.   Recognition: Every councilor desiring to speak should first address the
chair, and await recognition to obtain the floor. No persons other than members
of the council and the person having the floor shall enter into any discussion,
either directly or through a member of the council, without the permission of
the presiding officer.
   C.   Requirement Of "Second" Before Debate: No motion shall be debated until
it has been seconded and announced by the presiding officer.
   D.   Public Input During Open Comment Period: Members of the public desiring
to address the mayor and council shall first be recognized by the presiding
officer and then state their name and address for the record. Each person shall
have up to three (3) minutes to present their comments. Groups with like
comments should choose a spokesperson who will present their joint remarks.
   E.   Questions Or Complaints Directed To City Manager: Councilors should
refer people with questions or complaints to the city manager, explaining that
if they are not satisfied with the results of that meeting, they should ask to
be put on the next council meeting agenda or present their issue during the
public input portion at the next council meeting.
   F.   Councilor Responses: City councilors normally should not directly
respond to a public comment during the public open comment period. Councilor
comments should be held until the councilor comment period later in the meeting
or referred to the city manager for a response at a subsequent time.
   G.   Public Comment During Public Hearings: Remarks shall be limited to the
question then under discussion. All remarks and questions shall be addressed to
the council as a whole and not to any individual councilor. Any remarks and
questions regarding personnel or administration of the city shall be referred
to the city manager by the presiding officer. The presiding officer may
redirect other questions to a city councilor or the city manager, as
appropriate.
   H.   Questions Of City Staff By Councilors: Every councilor may address
questions directly to the city manager, who may either answer the inquiry or
designate a staff member to do so. Councilors are encouraged to present their
questions to the city manager prior to the meeting, when possible.
   I.   Restating Motion: Prior to a vote, the presiding officer shall restate
the motion or have the maker of the motion restate it to assure clarity of the
issue.
   J.   Voting: When a quorum is present, a majority of the council present and
voting shall decide a motion. Each councilor's vote shall be recorded
individually. A councilor who is present but abstains from voting is still
counted in the quorum. A councilor must be present to vote.
   K.   Abstentions: Councilors should abstain from voting only when they have
a conflict of interest or are not well informed on the issue that is being
voted upon.
   L.   Tie Votes: A motion fails in the event of a tie vote.
   M.   Reconsideration: A councilor who votes on the prevailing side of a
motion may move for reconsideration of any vote. This motion must occur during
the meeting or at the very next scheduled council meeting.
   N.   Anonymous Communications: Anonymous and unsigned communications shall
not be introduced in council meetings. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
1-5-6: DECORUM AND ORDER:
   A.   Presiding Officer: The presiding officer shall preserve decorum and
decide all points of order, subject to appeal to the council.
   B.   Conduct Of Councilors: The councilors shall help the presiding officer
preserve decorum during council meetings and shall not, by conversation or
other action, delay or interrupt the proceedings or refuse to follow the
directions of the presiding officer or these council rules. Councilors shall,
when addressing staff or members of the public, confine themselves to questions
or issues then under discussion, shall not engage in personal attack, shall not
impugn the motives of any speaker, and shall at all times, while in session or
otherwise, conduct themselves in a manner appropriate to the dignity of their
office.
   C.   City Staff And Employees: Members of the administrative staff,
employees of the city and other persons attending council meetings shall
observe the same rules of procedure, decorum and good conduct applicable to the
members of the council.
   D.   Unruly Behavior Of Attendees:
      1.   Any person who makes personal, impertinent, slanderous or
unauthorized remarks or who becomes boisterous while addressing the council or
attending a council meeting may be removed from the room, after fair warning,
if the presiding officer so directs. In case the presiding officer should fail
to act, any member of the council may obtain the floor and move to require
enforcement of this rule. Upon affirmative vote of the majority of the council
present, the person or persons shall be removed as if the presiding officer so
directed. Stamping of the feet, whistles, yells and clapping are similarly not
permitted.
      2.   Such person or persons may be barred from further audience before
the council and, in aggravated cases, an appropriate complaint shall be issued
by the presiding officer to prosecute this person or persons.
   E.   Disruption By Audience: If a meeting is disrupted by members of the
audience, the mayor may order that the council chamber be cleared and a recess
called until order is restored. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
1-5-7: CENSURE:
   A.   Authority To Discipline Council Member: The council has the inherent
right to make and enforce its own rules and to ensure compliance with those
laws generally applicable to public bodies. Should any councilor act in any
manner constituting a substantial violation of these rules or other general
laws, the council, acting as a whole, may discipline that councilor to the
extent provided by law, including public reprimand.
   B.   Investigation: To exercise such inherent right, the council has the
right to investigate the actions of any member of the council. Such
investigation shall be referred to the council as a whole in executive session
to discuss any finding that reasonable grounds exist that a substantial
violation has occurred.
   C.   Information Confidential: No individual councilor shall have the right
to make public any information obtained through such investigation. (Ord. 600,
12-1-1999)
1-5-8: CODE OF ETHICS:
   A.   Ethical Conduct: Councilors are encouraged to conduct themselves so as
to bring credit upon the city as a whole, and to set an example of good ethical
conduct for all citizens of the community. Councilors should constantly bear in
mind these responsibilities to the entire electorate, and refrain from actions
benefiting any individual or special interest group at the expense of the city
as a whole. Councilors should likewise do everything in their power to ensure
impartial application of the law to all citizens, and equal treatment of each
citizen before the law, without regard to race, national origin, sex, age,
social station or economic position.
   B.   Present Majority Position Of Council: If the mayor or a councilor
represents the city before another public body, governmental agency, community
organization or with the media, the mayor or councilor should always present
the majority position of the council. Personal opinions and comments may be
expressed only if it includes clarification that these statements do not
represent the position of the city council.
   C.   Representing Another Councilor's View: A councilor needs to have
another councilor's concurrence before representing that councilor's view or
position with the media, if it is different from the majority. (Ord. 600, 12-1-
1999)
1-5-9: COUNCIL RELATIONS WITH CITY STAFF:
   A.   Respect Those With Opposing Views: There will be mutual respect from
both staff and councilors of their respective roles and responsibilities when
and if expressing criticism in a public meeting.
   B.   Policies And Goals: The council sets city policies and goals. The staff
implements and administers the policies and goals.
   C.   Requests For Information: During a city council meeting, all requests
for information go directly to the mayor or city manager. At other times, if
the request for information would entail an effort that would require time to
be spent in researching and/or preparing a response, the request goes directly
to the city manager. The city manager will direct them to the other staff, the
city attorney or deal with them him/herself as appropriate. Questions or
complaints regarding staff go directly to the mayor or city manager.
   D.   Councilor Concerns Regarding City Staff: The city councilors may seek
information from staff members regarding the operation of their department, but
will not attempt to change or interfere with the operation or practice of any
city department or personnel, except by directing their concerns to the city
manager. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
1-5-10: COMMITTEES:
   A.   Appointment By Mayor: Board, commission, committee and task force
members are appointed by the mayor.
   B.   Budget Committee: The budget committee shall consist of seven (7)
resident lay members and the members of the city council for a total of
fourteen (14). The budget committee shall annually select a committee chair,
vice chair and secretary. The lay members' terms shall be three (3) years,
overlapping.
   C.   Planning Commission 1 : The planning commission shall consist of five
(5) persons with four (4) year overlapping terms. The members of the planning
commission shall annually, during the first meeting of the calendar year,
select a chair and vice chair. A staff member shall serve to keep the minutes
of each meeting.
   D.   Recreation Advisory Committee 2 : The recreation advisory committee
shall consist of five (5) persons with two (2) year overlapping terms. The
committee shall annually, during their first meeting of the calendar year,
select a chair and vice chair. A staff representative shall keep the minutes of
each meeting.
   E.   Task Force: A task force may be appointed for the length of time
necessary to accomplish their mission. The appropriate number of appointees may
be determined at the time of appointment.
   F.   Qualifications: All appointees to city boards, commissions or
committees shall be registered electors, and shall have resided in the city for
a period of at least one year. Task force members may be appointed from inside
and outside the city limits but should be involved in the city in some way,
such as with a business located within the city.
   G.   Removal Of Members: The mayor may remove a member from any city
committee or commission prior to the expiration of the term of office. Reasons
for removal may include, but are not limited to: 1) missing three (3)
consecutive regular meetings of the committee or commission; 2) disruptive or
inappropriate behavior prior to, during, or after committee or commission
meetings which prohibit the advisory body from completing its business in a
timely manner; or 3) not acting in the best interest of the citizens or city.
   H.   Attempts To Influence Members: Members of the council will not attempt
to lobby or influence board, committee, task force or commission members on any
item under their consideration. It is important for the advisory bodies to make
objective recommendations to the council on items before them. Councilors that
attempt to influence board, committee, task force or commission members on an
item may prejudice or hinder their role in reviewing the recommendation as a
member of the council. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 2, chapter 1 of this code.
2 2. See also title 2, chapter 3 of this code.
1-5-11: CONFIDENTIALITY:
   A.   Repeating Embarrassing Comments: Councilors will not repeat by name to
persons not on the council what others have said in a way that might embarrass
fellow councilors.
   B.   Matters Confidential Under Law: Councilors must keep in complete
confidence all written materials and verbal information provided to them on
matters that are confidential under law, to ensure that the city's position is
not compromised. No mention of information read or heard should be made to
anyone other than other councilors, the city manager or city attorney.
   C.   Executive Sessions: If the council, in executive session, provides
opinions or information to staff on proposed terms and conditions for any type
of negotiation whether it be related to property acquisition or disposal, a
proposed, pending or likely claim or litigation, and/or employee negotiations,
all contact with the other parties shall be made by the designated staff
representative handling the negotiations or litigation. A councilor shall not
have any contact or discussion with the other party or its representative
involved with the issue nor communicate any discussion conducted in executive
session.
   D.   Public Statements: All public statements, information or press releases
on confidential matters will be handled by the designated staff or council
spokesperson. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
1-5-12: SUSPENSION OR AMENDMENT OF RULES:
   A.   Temporary Suspension: Any provision of these rules not governed by
state law, the city charter or city code may be temporarily suspended by a
majority vote of the council.
   B.   Amendments: Amendments, deletions or additions to these council rules
shall be by ordinance approved by the city council. (Ord. 600, 12-1-1999)
CHAPTER 6
PERSONNEL RULES
SECTION:
1-6-1: Purpose
1-6-2: Adoption And Amendment Of Rules
1-6-3: Administration Of Rules
1-6-1: PURPOSE:
This chapter is adopted to establish an equitable and uniform procedure for
dealing with personnel matters, to attract to municipal service and to retain
the best and most competent persons available, to assure that appointments and
promotions of employees will be based on merit and fitness, and to provide a
reasonable degree of job security for qualified employees. (1996 Code §
2.08.010)
1-6-2: ADOPTION AND AMENDMENT OF RULES:
Personnel rules shall be adopted and amended by resolution or motion of the
city council. The rules shall provide means to recruit, select, develop, and
maintain an effective and responsive work force, and shall include policies and
procedures for employee hiring and advancements, training and career
development, job classification, salary administration, retirement, fringe
benefits, discipline, discharge, and other related activities. All appointments
and promotions shall be made in accordance with the personnel rules without
regard to sex, race, color, age, religion, political affiliation, national
origin, physical handicap, or marital status; and, furthermore, shall be based
on merit and fitness. (1996 Code § 2.08.020; amd. 2004 Code)
1-6-3: ADMINISTRATION OF RULES:
The city manager shall be responsible for:
   A.   Administering all the provisions of this chapter and of the personnel
rules not specifically reserved to the city council.
   B.   Preparing or causing to be prepared and recommending to the city
council personnel rules and revisions and amendments to such rules. (1996 Code
§ 2.08.030)
CHAPTER 7
ELECTIONS
SECTION:
1-7-1: Filing For City Office
1-7-2: Regulation Of Elections
1-7-3: State Election Laws Adopted
1-7-1: FILING FOR CITY OFFICE:
Candidates for city office file under Oregon Revised Statutes chapters 221 and
249, or any similar successor statute. (2004 Code)
1-7-2: REGULATION OF ELECTIONS:
When the charter of the city and this code do not provide a method of procedure
regarding regular and special elections, state law shall apply. (2004 Code)
1-7-3: STATE ELECTION LAWS ADOPTED:
State election laws are hereby adopted by reference, as provided in Oregon
Revised Statutes, as noted, or any similar successor statutes: title 23
"Elections"; chapter 249, "Candidates, Recall"; chapter 250 "Initiative And
Referendum"; chapter 254 "Conduct Of Elections"; and chapter 260 "Campaign
Finance Regulations, Election Offenses". (2004 Code)
CHAPTER 8
RECORDS
SECTION:
1-8-1: Records Management Program
1-8-2: Records Officer Designated; Duties
1-8-3: Records Manual Adopted
1-8-4: Records Retention Schedule Adopted
1-8-5: Inspection Of Records
1-8-6: Integrity Of Records
1-8-7: Postponing Release For Legal Opinion
1-8-8: Fees
1-8-1: RECORDS MANAGEMENT PROGRAM:
The city council hereby determines that it is in the best interest of the city
to have a records officer and records management program and, by this section,
state such intent and election to participate in the records management program
as defined by the state archivist. (Ord. 616, 6-5-2002)
1-8-2: RECORDS OFFICER DESIGNATED; DUTIES:
Pursuant to the conditions set forth in Oregon Revised Statutes 192.105, each
state agency and political subdivision shall designate a records officer to
coordinate its records management program and to serve as liaison with the
state archivist. The city manager or city manager's designee is hereby
designated as the records officer for the city and shall have the following
duties: (Ord. 616, 6-5-2002; amd. 2004 Code)
   A.   To create, maintain, monitor and update the city wide records retention
schedule through coordination with the state archivist and department
supervisors;
   B.   To create a records management manual providing for the proper records
handling, retention and storage for all city departments;
   C.   To assist in establishing storage facilities;
   D.   To keep updated on records law and procedures in order to implement
required procedures and/or educate staff regarding records retention; and
   E.   To report to the state archivist regarding the records management
program as required. (Ord. 616, 6-5-2002)
1-8-3: RECORDS MANUAL ADOPTED:
The city council hereby finds and determines that it is in the best interest of
the city to adopt the "Records Management Manual" as the official city records
management manual in its entirety and continue participation in the records
management program as defined by the state archivist. (Ord. 616, 6-5-2002)
1-8-4: RECORDS RETENTION SCHEDULE ADOPTED:
The city council finds and determines that it is in the best interest of the
city to adopt the "Records Retention Schedule" document as the official city
records retention schedule in its entirety and to continue participation in the
records management program as defined by the state archivist. The city manager
or his/her designee shall sign the certification of destruction prior to the
destruction of records. (Ord. 616, 6-5-2002)
1-8-5: INSPECTION OF RECORDS:
   A.   Right Of Inspection:
      1.   Every person has the right to inspect any nonexempt public record of
the city, subject to reasonable procedures.
      2.   The city shall provide proper and reasonable opportunities for
inspection and examination of the records during usual business hours if such
request does not interfere with the regular discharge of duties.
      3.   The city will not mail a general category of records to any public
or private entity, as it considers such an activity an unreasonable
interference with the regular discharge of its duties as the custodian (in
accordance with Oregon Revised Statutes 192.430). (1996 Code § 2.12.040)
   B.   Conditions Of Inspection: Records of any city departments may be
inspected under the following conditions:
      1.   A written request must be received by the city not less than two (2)
days prior to the desired date of inspection.
      2.   The specific record must be identified by type, case or date of the
record.
      3.   The person who will inspect the records must be identified by name.
(1996 Code § 2.12.050)
1-8-6: INTEGRITY OF RECORDS:
Staff shall take reasonable measures to preserve the integrity of city records
and maintain office efficiency and order: (1996 Code § 2.12.060)
   A.   The public records law allows for the inspection of the original
record. (Ord. 573, 8-7-1996; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Before releasing a public record for inspection, a staff member must
review the document to make certain the record does not contain any exempt
information.
   C.   A staff member should remain present while any original public record
is being inspected to ensure the protection of the document.
   D.   Copies may be furnished in lieu of inspection of original document.
(1996 Code § 2.12.060)
1-8-7: POSTPONING RELEASE FOR LEGAL OPINION:
A request for public records disclosure may be postponed if staff needs to
consult with the city attorney's office to obtain legal advice prior to
release. (1996 Code § 2.12.070)
1-8-8: FEES:
   A.   Determination Of Fees:
      1.   Fees shall be established to reimburse the city for its actual cost
in making public records available. Such calculation shall include cost of
summarizing, compiling, or tailoring a record, either by organizing or
transferring the record to a different medium, to meet the person's request.
Actual cost includes the time spent by staff in locating the requested records,
reviewing the records in order to delete exempt material, supervising the
inspection of original documents, and copying the records.
      2.   Staff should estimate charges for responding to a records request
and require prepayment of the estimated charges before acting on a request.
This is advisable as requests may require extensive staff time to locate or
process records. If the actual charges are less than the prepayment, any
overpayment must promptly be refunded.
      3.   Copies of documents provided by a routine file search will be
charged at the standard fee schedule unless subsection A4 of this section
applies.
      4.   In the event that the standard fee schedule does not accurately
reflect the actual cost of providing the records, such as when a request is for
an extraordinary number of documents or requires extra time to locate the
records, actual staff time should be charged. (1996 Code § 2.12.080)
   B.   Fee Schedule: A fee schedule for copies of public records of the city
shall be adopted by the council by resolution. (1996 Code § 2.12.090)
CHAPTER 9
DISPOSITION OF PROPERTY
SECTION:
1-9-1: Request For Disposal
1-9-2: Notice Of Sale; Reclamation Of Property
1-9-3: Officials And Employees Excluded From Bidding
1-9-4: Conduct Of Sale; Proceeds
1-9-5: City Use Or Donation
1-9-6: Inventory Searches Of Impounded Vehicles And Property
1-9-7: Surplus Personal Property
1-9-1: REQUEST FOR DISPOSAL:
Whenever the chief of police has any property, including money, in his custody,
the ownership of which is unknown, and which is unclaimed for sixty (60) days
after the property came into his custody, he shall report the fact to the city
manager and request authority to dispose of it as provided in this chapter.
(1996 Code § 2.16.010; amd. 2004 Code)
1-9-2: NOTICE OF SALE; RECLAMATION OF PROPERTY:
   A.   Action Upon Request: The city council shall act upon the request of the
city manager within thirty (30) days after the receipt of the request.
   B.   Disposal By Public Sale; Notice: If the request is to have the property
disposed of by public sale and if the council approves the request, the city
manager shall post written or printed notice of sale in three (3) public places
within the city, and place an advertisement of such notice in a local newspaper
of general circulation at least ten (10) days before the sale. The notice shall
describe the property, including money, and shall state the time and place of
public sale at which the property may be purchased by the highest bidder. (1996
Code § 2.16.020; amd. 2004 Code)
   C.   Reclamation Of Property: Until the date of the sale, the property,
including money, may be claimed at the office of the chief of police. If
ownership is proved, the chief of police shall turn the property, including
money, over to the owner and cancel the sale insofar as the particular claimed
property is concerned. (1996 Code § 2.16.020)
1-9-3: OFFICIALS AND EMPLOYEES EXCLUDED FROM BIDDING:
Members of the city government, including officials and employees, shall not be
allowed to bid at the sale. (1996 Code § 2.16.030)
1-9-4: CONDUCT OF SALE; PROCEEDS:
The chief of police shall conduct the sale and shall deposit the proceeds
thereof, after deducting the cost of the sale, together with any other money
included in the notice, in the city treasury to the credit of the city general
fund. (1996 Code § 2.16.040)
1-9-5: CITY USE OR DONATION:
In lieu of a sale of the property under the foregoing provisions of this
chapter, the city manager, with the approval of the city council, may transfer
any portion of unclaimed property to the city for use by the city, or may give
the unclaimed property to a worthy charity. (1996 Code § 2.16.050; amd. 2004
Code)
1-9-6: INVENTORY SEARCHES OF IMPOUNDED VEHICLES AND PROPERTY:
The city council is hereby authorized to adopt by order or resolution a policy
for inventory searches of impounded vehicles and property. (Ord. 624, 10-8-
2003)
1-9-7: SURPLUS PERSONAL PROPERTY:
Disposition of surplus personal property shall be made at the discretion of the
contracting agency under provisions of the state of Oregon public contracting
code, model rules, or the provisions of this section.
   A.   The contracting agency shall have the authority to declare personal
property owned by the city of Clatskanie to be surplus to the needs of the
city, and shall dispose of surplus property by one of the following methods:
      1.   Sell at public auction. The city may utilize a contracting firm,
approved by the contract review board, for disposition of the property on terms
and conditions contained in a contract approved by the contract review board.
The contracting agency shall give notice of the public auction by posting
notice of the means by which the property will be disposed by advertisement in
a newspaper of general circulation. Sale shall be for cash to the highest
responsible bidder.
      2.   Trade in on the purchase of replacement equipment or related
supplies.
      3.   Sell at a fixed price if doing so will result in substantially
greater net revenue to the city.
      4.   Contract for use, operation or maintenance by one or more private or
public entities. Prior to the approval of such a contract, the contracting
agency shall determine that the contract will promote the economic development
of the city.
   B.   All proceeds of the sale shall be paid to the city's general fund or
appropriate enterprise fund, subject to the terms and conditions of the
contract (if any) approved by the contract review board between the city of
Clatskanie and a firm selected to conduct the auction.
   C.   All personal property sold pursuant to this section shall be sold as is
without any warranty, either express or implied, of any kind, including, but
not limited to, warranties of title or fitness for any purpose. Upon receiving
payment for the personal property from the successful bidder, the contracting
agency or firm conducting an auction shall execute an appropriate bill of sale,
which shall recite that the sale is without warranty, as provided in this
section. (Ord. 638, 3-2-2005)
CHAPTER 10
FINANCIAL PROVISIONS
ARTICLE A. CONTRACTS AND PURCHASING
SECTION:
1-10A-1: Adoption Of Oregon Public Contracting Code
1-10A-2: Public Contracts; Designation Of Authority
1-10A-3: Compliance With Oregon Public Contracting Code
1-10A-4: Exemptions From Competitive Procurement
1-10A-5: Contracting Agency Authority
1-10A-6: Public Improvement Contracts
1-10A-7: Public Improvement Contract Negotiation
1-10A-8: Personal Service Contracts
1-10A-9: Purchasing Goods And Services
1-10A-1: ADOPTION OF OREGON PUBLIC CONTRACTING CODE:
In the event of a conflict between any provision of the state of Oregon public
contracting code, model rules, this article, or city policies, the provisions
of the state of Oregon contracting code and the model rules shall control.
(Ord. 638, 3-2-2005)
1-10A-2: PUBLIC CONTRACTS; DESIGNATION OF AUTHORITY:
The Clatskanie city council is designated as the local "contract review board"
under the state of Oregon public contracting code. The contract review board
may, from time to time, delegate its powers and responsibilities consistent
with the Oregon public contracting code, the model rules, or this code. The
city manager, or his/her designated agent, is designated as the city's
"contracting agency" for purposes of contracting powers and duties assigned to
the city of Clatskanie as a contracting agency under the state of Oregon public
contracting code or the model rules. (Ord. 638, 3-2-2005)
1-10A-3: COMPLIANCE WITH OREGON PUBLIC CONTRACTING CODE:
Except as specifically provided herein, public contracts shall be let by the
city of Clatskanie according to the state of Oregon public contracting code,
including the model rules adopted by the Oregon attorney general as they now
exist and as they may be amended in the future, and city policies and
regulations. Definitions provided by the state of Oregon public contracting
code or the model rules shall apply to city of Clatskanie procurements. (Ord.
638, 3-2-2005)
1-10A-4: EXEMPTIONS FROM COMPETITIVE PROCUREMENT:
The following classes of public contracts, goods, and services are hereby
exempted from competitive procurement:
   A.   Any contract exempted by the state of Oregon public contracting code or
model rules.
   B.   Change orders or contract amendments that are reasonably related to the
scope of work under the original contract, up to fifty thousand dollars
($50,000.00). Change orders or other amendments that increase the initial price
of the contract by more than fifty thousand dollars ($50,000.00) must be
separately approved by the contract review board.
   C.   Contracts for the purchase of the following: computer equipment and
software; works of art; products and supplies under five thousand dollars
($5,000.00).
   D.   Purchases made through federal programs, pursuant to Oregon Revised
Statutes 279A.180.
   E.   Purchases made based on state of Oregon price agreements for government
entities and the federal government purchasing alliance for U.S. communities.
   F.   An emergency contract, provided that the contracting agency adheres to
the requirements of Oregon Revised Statutes 279B.080 or 279C.335(5), model
rules, and city policies.
   G.   Any other contract (including sole source and brand name specification
contracts) where the public interest would be promoted by exempting the
contract from the competitive bidding process, provided that the contract
review board adheres to the public contracting code and the model rules in
making the exemption. (Ord. 638, 3-2-2005)
1-10A-5: CONTRACTING AGENCY AUTHORITY:
The contracting agency has contracting authority and responsibilities as
follows to:
   A.   Enter into city contacts for budgeted expenditures and approve change
orders and amendments without additional authorization of the contract review
board, so long as the contract, change order, or amendment does not exceed
fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00).
   B.   Recommend that the contract review board approve or disapprove contract
awards in excess of fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00), or change orders or
amendments to contracts of more than fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00).
   C.   Consistent with this code, adopt forms, procedures, and administrative
regulations for all city purchases.
   D.   Enter into contracts or permits for local concessions and street
vendors (pursuant to applicable city policy) where the annual amount to be paid
to or by the city is not expected to exceed fifteen thousand dollars
($15,000.00) per year.
   E.   Enter into contracts or procure goods and services in the event of an
emergency in accordance with city policies and procedures adopted by the city
council. (Ord. 638, 3-2-2005; amd. Ord. 699. 9-2-2020)
1-10A-6: PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT CONTRACTS:
A public improvement contract does not include contracts for minor alterations,
ordinary repair and maintenance of public improvements, contracts for projects
for which no substantial city funds are directly or indirectly used except for
participation that is incidental or related primarily to project design or
inspection, and does not include any other construction contract that is not
defined as a public improvement under state law. A public improvement contract
may be let under the following procedures:
   A.   Public improvements valued at less than five thousand dollars
($5,000.00) may be awarded by the contracting agency based on informal quotes.
   B.   Public improvements valued at five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) or more
but not more than fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00) may be awarded by the
contracting agency based on written quotations. At least three (3) written
quotations shall be obtained if reasonably possible.
   C.   The contracting agency shall award a contract under this section to the
prospective contractor whose quote will best serve the interests of the city of
Clatskanie, taking into account price and other applicable factors, such as
experience, specific expertise, availability, project understanding, contractor
capacity, and contractor responsibility. If the contract is not awarded on the
basis of the lowest price, the contracting agency shall make a written record
of the basis for the award.
   D.   Public improvements valued at more than fifteen thousand dollars
($15,000.00) may be awarded by the contracting review board after a formal
solicitation of sealed bids in accordance with Oregon Revised Statutes 279C.
   E.   A procurement may not be artificially divided or fragmented to qualify
for the informal contract award procedures provided by this section.
   F.   A public improvement contract let under this section may be amended by
change order in accordance with this article and city policy. (Ord. 638, 3-2-
2005)
1-10A-7: PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT CONTRACT NEGOTIATION:
If bids are solicited for a public improvement contract, and all bids exceed
the budget for the project, the contracting agency may, prior to contract
award, negotiate for a price within the project budget under the following
procedures:
   A.   Negotiations will begin with the lowest, responsive and responsible
bidder. If negotiations are not successful, then the contracting agency may
begin negotiations with the second lowest responsive, responsible bidder, and
so on.
   B.   Negotiations may include the inclusion of value engineering and other
options to attempt to bring the project cost within the budgeted amount.
   C.   A contract may not be awarded under this section if the scope of the
project is significantly changed from the description in the original bid
documents.
   D.   The contracting agency will adhere to the public records provisions of
Oregon Revised Statutes 279C.340 in applying this section. (Ord. 638, 3-2-2005)
1-10A-8: PERSONAL SERVICE CONTRACTS:
Personal service contracts may be let in compliance with state law and under
the following procedures:
   A.   Personal service contracts shall be used for retaining the services for
the following classes of service contracts. Nothing in this section shall apply
to employment of regular city employees. The contracting agency shall have
discretion to determine whether specific services contracts or additional
classes of services not specifically mentioned below fit within the definition
of personal services. The following shall be considered personal services
contracts:
      1.   Services that require special training or certification, skill,
technical, creative, professional, or communication skills;
      2.   Services that require unique or specialized knowledge, the exercise
of independent judgment, and the quality of service depends on attributes
unique to the service provider;
      3.   Independent contractors generally;
      4.   Architect services;
      5.   Engineering services;
      6.   Land surveyors;
      7.   "Personal services" defined by ORS 279C.100(5);
      8.   "Related services" as defined by ORS 279C.100(8);
      9.   Auditor services;
      10.   City attorney, special counsel, or any other attorney services;
      11.   Code enforcement services;
      12.   Artists, designers, and performers;
      13.   Computer, web development, networking, and programming services;
      14.   Licensed professionals;
      15.   Consultants;
      16.   Property managers; or
      17.   Other service contracts determined by the contracting agency to be
personal service contracts.
   B.   For personal service contracts valued at five thousand dollars
($5,000.00) or less per year, the contracting agency may negotiate and execute
a contract for such services with any qualified contractor of his or her
selection.
   C.   For personal service contracts valued at more than five thousand
dollars ($5,000.00) but not more than fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00) per
year, the contracting agency shall solicit at least three (3) prospective
contractors who shall appear to have at least minimum qualifications for the
proposed assignment, notify each prospective contractor in reasonable detail of
the proposed assignment, and determine the prospective contractor's interest
and ability to perform the proposed assignment. Following a review of the
qualifications and interview, where conducted, of the interested prospective
contractors, the contracting agency shall select the prospective contractor,
and shall prepare a personal service contract.
   D.   For personal service contracts valued at more than fifteen thousand
dollars ($15,000.00) per year, the contract review board may award a contract
after a formal solicitation and advertisement for sealed proposals.
   E.   The following criteria should be considered in the evaluation and
selection of contractor for a personal service contract valued at more than
fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00) per year:
      1.   Specialized experience in the type of work to be performed, and
capacity and capability to perform the work, including any specialized services
within the time limitations for the work.
      2.   Educational and professional record, including past record of
performance on contracts with governmental agencies and private parties with
respect to cost control, quality of work, ability to meet schedules, and
contract administration, where applicable.
      3.   Availability to perform the assignment and familiarity with the area
in which the specific work is located, including knowledge of design or
techniques peculiar to it, where applicable.
      4.   Any other factors relevant to the particular contract.
   F.   The selection procedures described in this section may be waived by the
contracting agency, at his or her discretion, where an emergency exists that
could not have been reasonably foreseen and requires such prompt execution of a
contract to remedy the situation that there is not sufficient time to permit
utilization of the selection procedures.
   G.   Nothing contained in this section shall preclude the city from
complying with provisions of federal or state law that require the city to
utilize a different selection or contracting procedure. (Ord. 638, 3-2-2005;
amd. Ord. 697, 4-1-2020)
1-10A-9: PURCHASING GOODS AND SERVICES:
The procurement of goods and services not determined to be public improvement
contracts or personal service contracts shall be made under the following
procedures:
   A.   For goods and services valued at less than five hundred dollars
($500.00), the contracting agency may purchase from any qualified vendor
according to city regulations.
   B.   For goods and services valued at more than five hundred dollars
($500.00) but not more than five thousand dollars ($5,000.00), the contracting
agency shall attempt to obtain three (3) quotations and document that the
selection made is in the best interest of the city.
   C.   For goods and services valued at more than five thousand dollars
($5,000.00) but not more than fifteen thousand dollars ($15,000.00), the
contracting agency shall purchase based on written quotations and documentation
that the selection made is in the best interest of the city. At least three (3)
written quotations shall be obtained if reasonably possible.
   D.   For goods and services valued at more than fifteen thousand dollars
($15,000.00), the contract review board shall purchase based on a
recommendation from the contracting agency. The recommendation shall be in
accordance with city policies and Oregon Revised Statutes chapter 279B and
shall document the quotations or proposals received and include a statement why
the selection is in the best interest of the city.
   E.   The city council may by resolution establish and revise purchasing
policies and procedures in compliance with this article and state law. (Ord.
638, 3-2-2005)
ARTICLE B. FUNDS
SECTION:
1-10B-1: Timber And Infrastructure Improvement Fund
1-10B-1: TIMBER AND INFRASTRUCTURE IMPROVEMENT FUND:
   A.   Fund Established: The timber and infrastructure improvement fund is
hereby established.
   B.   Vote Of Council: Five (5) members of the city council shall constitute
a two-thirds (2/3) vote for purposes of this section.
   C.   Disposition Of Revenues:
      1.   All revenue from interest on timber harvesting within the city's
watershed property shall be dedicated to the timber and infrastructure
improvement fund, except for timberlands currently dedicated for the benefit of
the Scout Lake recreation area and city cemetery expansion.
      2.   All resources and expenditures shall be budgeted and expended
according to the local budget law 1  and generally accepted accounting
principles. All expenditures shall be classified as either "principal" or
"projects", and each such expenditure category is hereby established with
restrictions.
      3.   The following are allowable expenditures classified as "principal":
         a.   The operations cost of harvesting, building and maintaining roads
for logging, reforestation, maintenance, management of the watershed, and
management of the timber and infrastructure improvement fund.
         b.   Council may loan to the general fund for operating expenses until
property taxes are received.
         c.   Any other loan or transfer from the timber and infrastructure
fund may be approved by council following a two-thirds (2/3) council vote after
a public hearing.
      4.   The following are allowable expenditures classified as "projects":
         a.   Each fiscal year a total of one hundred twenty five thousand
dollars ($125,000.00) or ninety percent (90%) of fund interest earnings on June
30 of the prior fiscal year, whichever is greater, may be expended for capital
projects for the water, sewer, and street (including storm drainage and
sidewalk) systems.
         b.   Any monies remaining in projects at the end of the fiscal year
shall be dedicated to projects for future use.
   D.   Annual Budget Document: The annual budget document shall contain a
twenty (20) year table projecting revenues and expenditures of the timber and
infrastructure improvement fund. (Ord. 622, 11-6-2002; amd. Ord. 638, 3-2-2005)
 
Notes
1 1. ORS 294.305 et seq.
CHAPTER 11
CITY CEMETERIES
SECTION:
1-11-1: Rules And Regulations; Council Authority
1-11-2: City Manager Powers And Duties
1-11-3: Operation And Maintenance
1-11-4: Permits For Interment, Removal Or Transfer
1-11-5: Cemetery Fund
1-11-6: Reserves Created
1-11-7: Lots And Graves
1-11-8: Cremains Lots
1-11-1: RULES AND REGULATIONS; COUNCIL AUTHORITY:
The city council shall adopt rules and regulations for the use, control,
operation and management of the city cemeteries. The rules and regulations may
be revised and amended as needed by resolution of the city council, to the
extent not inconsistent with this chapter. (1996 Code § 2.20.010)
1-11-2: CITY MANAGER POWERS AND DUTIES:
The city manager or his designee shall receive, issue proper receipts for, and
place in appropriate accounts, reserves or funds, all monies due the city from
the sale of lots, services furnished, and all other sources. The city shall
issue in the name of the city, and shall keep complete records of, all matters
pertaining to the cemeteries, including a record of ownership of lots and
graves. (1996 Code § 2.20.020; amd. 2004 Code)
1-11-3: OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE:
   A.   Authority: The operation and maintenance of the cemeteries shall be the
responsibility of the public works department, subject to the general
supervision of the city manager. Maintenance services may be provided by city
personnel, independent contract, and volunteers, as shall be considered
reasonable and necessary by the city council. (1996 Code § 2.20.030)
   B.   Budget; Enterprise Fund: The city cemeteries shall be operated as a
business enterprise and shall be budgeted as an enterprise fund. (1996 Code §
2.20.040)
1-11-4: PERMITS FOR INTERMENT, REMOVAL OR TRANSFER:
   A.   Compliance With State Statutes, Regulations: The interment, removal and
transfer of bodies shall be governed by the applicable statutes and regulations
of the state. The city manager shall periodically review cemetery records to
assure accurate documentation and compliance with state regulations. (1996 Code
§ 2.20.050)
   B.   Disinterment: Any disinterment may require approval from the state of
Oregon and survivor(s). (Ord. 644, 3-1-2006)
1-11-5: CEMETERY FUND:
A separate cemetery fund with supporting ledgers and journals shall account for
all reserve accounts, income and expenditures of the city cemeteries. (1996
Code § 2.20.060)
1-11-6: RESERVES CREATED:
   A.   Endowment Reserve: For the purpose of providing for the perpetual care
and maintenance of lots and graves of city cemeteries, there is created an
"endowment reserve", to be so named. Fifty percent (50%) of all revenues from
the sale of cemetery lots shall be placed in the endowment reserve. The
endowment reserve may be invested in the same manner as is allowed by state law
for public funds. The interest only from investment of the endowment reserve
may be appropriated as a resource of the cemetery operating budget. (1996 Code
§ 2.20.070)
   B.   Expansion Reserve: For the purpose of providing for capital
improvements and expansion of city cemeteries, there is created an "expansion
reserve", to be so named. Revenues from the sale of timber harvested on
cemetery property and such other revenues as the city council may wish to
commit to future improvements may be placed in the expansion reserve. Principal
and interest may be appropriated as the city council deems necessary. (1996
Code § 2.20.080)
1-11-7: LOTS AND GRAVES:
   A.   Prices And Charges: The city council shall, by resolution, establish
the schedules of prices to be charged for lots, graves, grave openings and
other services and privileges; provided, however, that the charges now being
made shall be continued until changed by resolution of the council. (1996 Code
§ 2.20.090)
   B.   Title Conveyance:
      1.   Every conveyance of a lot in the cemeteries shall be by certificate
of right of interment executed by the city manager, but such conveyance shall
only have the effect of giving the perpetual use of a lot for burial, subject
to the laws of the state and the ordinances of the city. (1996 Code § 2.20.100;
amd. Ord. 644, 3-1-2006)
      2.   No grave or lot which has been conveyed by the city can be sold,
transferred, assigned or exchanged for other graves except with the consent of
the city manager and upon such terms and conditions as the city manager may
provide. Notice in writing of such consent and the conditions thereof shall be
mailed or otherwise delivered to the person concerned by the city manager.
(1996 Code § 2.20.100)
   C.   Owner Privileges:
      1.   The owner of a grave in any improved portion of the cemeteries will
be allowed to remove the body from the grave and reinter it in any other grave
in the cemetery which he may own, and will be allowed the price paid for such
relinquished grave.
      2.   The owner of a lot may, with the approval of the city manager, allow
the burial of a friend or any other person in such lot, but to allow such
burial for any compensation is strictly forbidden. (1996 Code § 2.20.110)
      3.   Subdivisions of graves or lots by owners is not allowed; however,
additional cremains may be placed in a lot according to cemetery rules and
regulations. (1996 Code § 2.20.110; amd. Ord. 644, 3-1-2006)
      4.   Planting of trees or shrubs shall be prohibited. (1996 Code §
2.20.110)
1-11-8: CREMAINS LOTS:
Areas may be specifically portioned off for the purpose of cremains burials.
(1996 Code § 2.20.120; amd. 2004 Code)
TITLE 2
BOARDS, COMMISSIONS AND COMMITTEES
CHAPTER 1
PLANNING COMMISSION
SECTION:
2-1-1: Commission Established; Membership
2-1-2: Term Of Office
2-1-3: Vacancies And Removals
2-1-4: Organization; Officers
2-1-5: Meetings
2-1-6: Powers And Duties
2-1-7: Unenumerated Duties
2-1-1: COMMISSION ESTABLISHED; MEMBERSHIP 1 :
   A.   Established: There is hereby reestablished a city planning commission
for the city. (1996 Code § 2.04.010)
   B.   Membership: The commission shall consist of five (5) members who are
not officials or employees of the city. The city manager shall be entitled to
sit with the commission and take part in its discussions, but shall not have
the right to vote. A council member may be appointed in a liaison capacity to
sit with the commission, but shall not have the right to vote. (1996 Code §
2.04.020)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection 1-5-10C of this code.
2-1-2: TERM OF OFFICE:
Members of the planning commission shall be appointed by the city council for a
term of four (4) years from the first calendar day of this year, except that
initial appointments of some members shall be for other specified terms in
order to establish an approximately equal expiration of terms each year. (1996
Code § 2.04.030)
2-1-3: VACANCIES AND REMOVALS:
   A.   Appointment For Remainder Of Term: Appointments to fill vacancies shall
be for the remainder of the unexpired term.
   B.   Removal For Misconduct; Hearing: A member may be removed by the city
council after hearing, for misconduct or nonperformance of duty.
   C.   Unexcused Absences; Removal After Hearing: A member who is absent from
three (3) consecutive meetings without an excuse as approved by the planning
commission is rebuttably presumed to be in nonperformance of duty and the city
council shall declare the position vacant unless finding otherwise following
the hearing. (1996 Code § 2.04.040)
2-1-4: ORGANIZATION; OFFICERS:
   A.   Presiding Members: At its first meeting of each calendar year, the
commission shall elect a chairman and vice chairman to serve one year terms.
(1996 Code § 2.04.050)
   B.   Staff Services; Records: The city manager shall provide a secretary to
the commission, and such other staff and consultation services as may be
appropriate. The secretary shall keep a record of commission meetings. (1996
Code § 2.04.060)
2-1-5: MEETINGS:
   A.   Quorum: A majority of members of the planning commission shall
constitute a quorum. A majority of those members actually voting is necessary
for any action to be taken by the commission.
   B.   Times For Holding Meetings; Open Meetings: The commission shall meet at
least once a month. Meetings of the commission shall be open to the public.
Meetings other than at regularly scheduled times may be announced at a prior
meeting and thereby made a part of the meeting records.
   C.   Calling Special Meetings; Notice: The chair, upon his own action or at
the request of two (2) members of the commission, shall, by giving notice to
members of the commission, call a previously unannounced special meeting of the
commission for a time not earlier than twenty four (24) hours after the notice
is given. Notice of a previously unannounced meeting shall be posted at the
city hall and, to the extent feasible, provided to interested persons at least
twenty four (24) hours prior to the meeting. (1996 Code § 2.04.070)
2-1-6: POWERS AND DUTIES:
The commission shall have the powers and duties which are assigned to it by
charter, ordinances or resolutions of the city and general laws of the state.
The duties of the commission shall include the following: (1996 Code §
2.04.080)
   A.   Comprehensive Development Plan: The commission shall:
      1.   Proceed with the preparation of a comprehensive development plan for
the city with due and deliberate consideration of the goals and guidelines of
the land conservation and development commission of the state of Oregon. Upon
completion, recommend the plan to the city council for adoption.
      2.   Subsequent to its adoption, base all its decisions relating to land
use, public facilities, circulation, community appearance, and similar matters
on the plan, and ensure that all matters affecting the development of the city
and its environs including, but not limited to, zoning, subdivisions, signs and
capital improvements shall conform to the plan.
      3.   Recommend to the city council ordinances (and amendments to existing
ordinances) intended to carry out the purposes, principles and proposals
expressed in the comprehensive development plan (such as zoning, subdivision
and the like).
      4.   Review ordinances in existence at the time of adoption of the
comprehensive development plan to ensure that they are not inconsistent with
the plan. (1996 Code § 2.04.080; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Subdivisions: The commission shall review and, subject to appeal, take
final action on proposed subdivisions and major or minor land partitionings.
   C.   Zoning: The commission shall review and, subject to appeal, take final
action on proposed variances, conditional uses or other deviations from the
city zoning ordinance as it now exists or is constituted in the future.
   D.   Studies: The commission shall conduct studies appropriate to an
understanding of area development and its significance to the public interest.
   E.   Capital Improvement Program: The commission shall prepare and
periodically review the city's capital improvement program, ensure that it is
consistent with the comprehensive development plan, and make recommendations as
appropriate to the common council.
   F.   Consult With Public Agencies: The commission shall consult and advise
with public agencies and private citizens on matters concerning the area within
six (6) miles of the city limits and the city's urban growth boundary.
   G.   Other Functions: The commission shall perform such other functions as
the city council may request.
   H.   Promotion Of Public Interest, Health, Safety: The commission shall
study and propose in general such measures as may be advisable for promotion of
the public interest, health, morals, safety, comfort, convenience and welfare
of the city and its environs. (1996 Code § 2.04.080)
2-1-7: UNENUMERATED DUTIES:
This chapter shall be liberally construed. The enumeration of duties in section
2-1-6 of this chapter is not intended to divest the planning commission of any
other duties or powers now imposed or authorized by law. (1996 Code § 2.04.090)
CHAPTER 2
URBAN RENEWAL AGENCY
SECTION:
2-2-1: Declaration
2-2-2: Authority
2-2-3: Purpose
2-2-4: Findings And Declarations
2-2-5: Establishment Of Agency
2-2-6: Agency Name; Procedures
2-2-1: DECLARATION:
This chapter is enacted for the purpose of declaring that the blighted areas
(as defined in Oregon Revised Statutes 457.010[1]) exist in the city, declaring
a need for an urban renewal area to function in the city, and electing to have
the powers of the urban renewal agency exercised by the city council. (Ord.
604, 2-7-2001)
2-2-2: AUTHORITY:
This chapter is adopted pursuant to the authority of Oregon Revised Statutes
chapter 457 and more particularly, the provisions of Oregon Revised Statutes
457.035 and 457.045. (Ord. 604, 2-7-2001)
2-2-3: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to establish the urban renewal agency of the
city as an operating agency exercising the powers granted to such an agency by
Oregon Revised Statutes chapter 457. Oregon Revised Statutes 457.035 creates a
public body corporate and politic in each municipality (defined as any county
or city in the state) to be known as the urban renewal agency of the
municipality. The urban renewal agency cannot exercise its powers until or
unless the governing body of the municipality declares that blighted areas (as
defined in Oregon Revised Statutes 457.010[1]) exist in the municipality and
that there is a need for an urban renewal agency to function in the
municipality; and the governing body elects to have the powers exercised in one
of the ways provided in Oregon Revised Statutes 457.045. (Ord. 604, 2-7-2001)
2-2-4: FINDINGS AND DECLARATIONS:
   A.   Generally: The city council finds and declares that blighted areas as
defined in Oregon Revised Statutes 457.010(1) exist in the city and that there
is a need for an urban renewal agency to function in the city.
   B.   Conditions Contributing To Blight: The city council finds the following
conditions have contributed to blight in the city as defined by Oregon Revised
Statutes 457.010(1)(b) and (1)(h):
      1.   The transition out of the traditional natural resource base economy,
which has resulted in a loss of timber and wood products jobs. (Source: OEDD)
      2.   The 1993 closure of the Trojan Nuclear Energy Plant, which caused a
loss of over four hundred (400) jobs.
      3.   The flood of 1996, which caused thirty six million dollars
($36,000,000.00) in public and private property loss and/or damage in the city
of Clatskanie and Columbia County. (Source: Col-Pac Economic Development
District)
Unknown damage due to flood such as damage to foundations and supporting
structures for downtown buildings.
      4.   The loss of the Beaver Lumber Company and seventy five (75) jobs due
to the flood of 1996.
      5.   The closure of other businesses due to the flood of 1996 and the
downturn in Clatskanie's economy.
      6.   The following dilapidated structures in the city including, but not
limited to:
         a.   The dock behind the city minimart;
         b.   The old IOOF building; and
         c.   The former Johnson Oil Gas Station that has suspected ground
contamination, which prevents new development.
      7.   Infrastructure inadequacies including, but not limited to:
         a.   No storm water drainage system;
         b.   Uneven and damaged sidewalks in the downtown area;
         c.   High water events cause reverse flow of water through drainage
culvert from the river into the city downtown parking lot; and
         d.   Flood protection is needed from high water events in two (2) or
three (3) areas.
      8.   Riverbank erosion throughout the downtown and the proposed urban
renewal area.
   C.   Agency Powers Exercised By Council: The city council elects to have the
powers of the urban renewal agency exercised by the city council acting as the
urban renewal agency of the city. (Ord. 604, 2-7-2001)
2-2-5: ESTABLISHMENT OF AGENCY:
The urban renewal agency of the city created by Oregon Revised Statutes 457.035
is hereby empowered by this chapter to exercise the powers granted to it by
Oregon Revised Statutes chapter 457. (Ord. 604, 2-7-2001)
2-2-6: AGENCY NAME; PROCEDURES:
The urban renewal agency of the city may be known as the Clatskanie development
agency. Such agency shall meet under the direction of the mayor of the city
within thirty (30) days from the effective date of this chapter to make
provision for meetings and to establish rules and regulations to govern its
procedures. Such agency may delegate such duties and responsibilities as it may
deem proper, prepare a budget and establish financial procedures, enter into
contracts and do all other things necessary to carry out the powers granted to
it by Oregon Revised Statutes chapter 457. Such powers shall be exercised in
accordance with and subject to Oregon Revised Statutes chapter 457 and other
applicable laws. (Ord. 604, 2-7-2001)

BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
BUSINESS LICENSES GENERALLY
SECTION:
