required in section
6-6B-3 of this article, or twenty four (24) hours after adoption of a
resolution declaring a vehicle to be a public nuisance as set forth in section
6-6B-5 of this article, the city shall be deemed to have acquired jurisdiction
to abate the nuisance and may remove the vehicle by use of city employees or
duly authorized independent contractors. It is unlawful for any person to
interfere with, hinder, or refuse to allow such persons to enter upon private
property for the purpose of removing a vehicle under the provisions of this
article.
   B.   Appraisal: After removing the vehicle, the city shall cause it to be
appraised. (1996 Code § 10.12.150)
6-6B-7: LOW VALUE VEHICLE:
   A.   Notice Of Intent To Dismantle: If the vehicle is appraised at seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) or less, the chief of police shall file with
the state department of motor vehicles an affidavit describing the vehicle,
including the license plates, if any, stating the location and appraised value
of the vehicle, and stating that the vehicle will be junked or dismantled. The
chief of police may, without notice and public auction, dispose of the vehicle
and execute a certificate of sale. (1996 Code § 10.12.160)
   B.   Certificate Of Sale: The certificate of sale shall be in such form as
determined by the city. (1996 Code § 10.12.160; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6B-8: PUBLIC SALE:
   A.   Notice:
      1.   If a vehicle is appraised over seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00), the chief of police shall cause to be published in a newspaper of
general circulation within the city a notice of sale. The notice of sale shall
state:
         a.   The sale is of discarded property in possession of the city;
         b.   The description of the vehicle, including the type, make, license
number, identification number, and any other information which will aid in
accurately identifying the vehicle;
         c.   The terms of the sale; and
         d.   The date, time and place of the sale.
      2.   The notice of sale shall be published two (2) times. The first
publication shall be made not less than ten (10) days prior to the date of the
proposed sale, and the second shall be made not less than three (3) days prior
to the date of the proposed sale. (1996 Code § 10.12.170)
   B.   Conducting Public Sale:
      1.   If a vehicle is appraised over seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00), the chief of police shall hold a sale at the time and place
appointed within the view of the vehicle to be sold.
      2.   The vehicle shall be sold to the highest and best bidder; provided,
that if no bids are entered or those bids which are entered are less than the
costs incurred by the city, the chief of police may enter a bid on behalf of
the city in an amount equal to such costs. (1996 Code § 10.12.180)
      3.   At the time of payment of the purchase price, the chief of police
shall execute a certificate of sale, in duplicate, the original of which shall
be delivered to the purchaser, and the copy thereof filed with the city.
      4.   The certificate of sale shall be in such form as determined by the
city. (1996 Code § 10.12.180; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6B-9: REDEMPTION BEFORE SALE:
   A.   Application For Vehicle Redemption: A vehicle, impounded under the
provisions of this article, may be redeemed by its owner or by the person in
charge of the property from which the vehicle was removed, before a sale or
disposition has taken place, by applying to the police department, whereupon he
shall:
      1.   Submit evidence of his ownership or interest in the vehicle,
satisfactory to the chief of police, that such claim is rightful; and
      2.   Pay the costs due and owing at the time the application to redeem is
made; and
      3.   Give evidence that the nuisance character of the vehicle will not be
allowed to resume.
   B.   Return Of Vehicle; Issuance Of Receipt: Upon compliance with subsection
A of this section, the chief of police shall execute a receipt and cause the
vehicle to be returned. (1996 Code § 10.12.190)
6-6B-10: ASSESSMENT OF COSTS:
   A.   Notice To Owner: After disposing of the discarded vehicle and deducting
the money, if any, received from any sale of the vehicle from the costs, the
city shall give notice as specified in section
6-6B-3 of this article to the person in charge of the property from which the
vehicle was removed:
      1.   Of the unpaid costs of abatement.
      2.   That the cost as indicated will be assessed to and become a lien
against the real property unless paid within thirty (30) days from the date of
the notice.
      3.   That if the person in charge of the property objects to the cost of
the abatement indicated, he may file a written notice of objection with the
city within twenty (20) days from the date of the notice. (1996 Code §
10.12.200; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Hearing Objections: Within forty (40) days after the date of the
notice, objections to the proposed assessment shall be heard and determined by
the council.
   C.   Resolution; Assessment Of Lien:
      1.   If the costs of the abatement are not paid within thirty (30) days
from the date of the notice, an assessment of the costs shall be made by
resolution of the city council and shall be entered in the docket of city
liens, and upon such entry being made shall constitute a lien upon the real
property from which the nuisance was removed or abated.
      2.   The lien shall be enforced in the same manner as liens for street
improvements are enforced, and shall bear interest at the rate of six percent
(6%) per annum. Such interest shall accrue from date of the entry of the lien
in the lien docket.
      3.   An error in the name of the person in charge of the property shall
not void the assessment nor will a failure to receive the notice of the
proposed assessment render the assessment void. The assessment shall remain a
valid lien against the property. (1996 Code § 10.12.200)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
PUBLIC RIGHTS OF WAY
SECTION:
7-1-1: Definitions
7-1-2: Jurisdiction
7-1-3: Scope Of Regulatory Control
7-1-4: City Permission Requirement
7-1-5: Obligation Of City
7-1-6: Vacation Of Rights Of Way
7-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following shall mean:
CITY: The city of Clatskanie, Oregon.
PERSON: Individual, corporation, association, firm, partnership, district,
joint stock company, and similar entities.
PUBLIC RIGHTS OF WAY: Includes, but is not limited to, streets, roads,
highways, bridges, alleys, sidewalks, trails, paths, bikeways, public easements
and all other public ways or areas, including subsurface and air space over
these areas.
WITHIN THE CITY: Territory over which the city now has or acquires jurisdiction
for the exercise of its powers. (Ord. 586, 5-5-1997)
7-1-2: JURISDICTION:
The city has jurisdiction and exercises regulatory control over all public
rights of way within the city under the authority of the city charter and state
law. (Ord. 586, 5-5-1997)
7-1-3: SCOPE OF REGULATORY CONTROL:
The city has jurisdiction and exercises regulatory control over each public
right of way whether the city has a fee, easement, or other legal interest in
the right of way. The city has jurisdiction and regulatory control over each
right of way whether the legal interest in the right of way was obtained by
grant, dedication, prescription, reservation, condemnation, annexation,
foreclosure or other means. (Ord. 586, 5-5-1997)
7-1-4: CITY PERMISSION REQUIREMENT:
No person may occupy or encroach on a public right of way without the
permission of the city. The city may grant permission to use rights of way by
franchises, licenses or permits. (Ord. 586, 5-5-1997)
7-1-5: OBLIGATION OF CITY:
The exercise of jurisdiction and regulatory control over a public right of way
by the city is not official acceptance of the right of way, and does not
obligate the city to maintain or repair any part of the right of way. (Ord.
586, 5-5-1997)
7-1-6: VACATION OF RIGHTS OF WAY:
   A.   Procedure: Vacation of any street, avenue, boulevard, alley, plat,
public square or other public place shall be in accordance with Oregon Revised
Statutes 271.080 through 271.230.
   B.   Fee: A right of way vacation application fee shall be paid upon the
filing of the petition for vacation. Such fee, which shall be sufficient to
cover the cost of publication, posting, and other anticipated expenses, shall
be established by resolution of the city council. (Ord. 583, 10-2-1996)
CHAPTER 2
STREET AND SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION
SECTION:
7-2-1: Authority To Establish Public Works Standards
7-2-2: Permit Required
7-2-3: Application For Permit
7-2-4: Issuance Of Permit
7-2-5: Work Under Permit; Approval Certificate
7-2-6: Record Of Permits
7-2-7: Width Of Streets And Sidewalks
7-2-8: Repairing Sidewalks
7-2-1: AUTHORITY TO ESTABLISH PUBLIC WORKS STANDARDS:
The city council may establish and revise public works standards by resolution.
(2004 Code)
7-2-2: PERMIT REQUIRED:
   A.   Permit Required; Exception: From and after the effective date hereof,
it is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to break up, dig up, cut,
excavate, remove or fill in any street or to construct any sidewalk, crosswalk
or gutter, plank roadway, or other roadway, or to do any work in or upon or
through any of the public streets within the corporate limits of the city
without first obtaining a written permit therefor as provided in this chapter;
except, that the provisions of this section shall not apply to any street or
sidewalk repair within the city limits authorized by law or made in pursuance
of a notice to repair from the city council. (1996 Code § 12.04.010)
   B.   Compliance With City Plans And Specifications: Any improvement not
provided for in this title shall be done in accordance with plans and
specifications approved by the city. (1996 Code § 12.04.010; amd. 2004 Code)
7-2-3: APPLICATION FOR PERMIT:
Any person, firm or corporation owning real property, or having same under
control as owner, agent or trustee, who may desire to do grading, to lay a
sidewalk, gutter or roadway, or to make any kind of street improvement in front
of said property, other than repair, within the limits authorized by law, or in
pursuance of a notice to repair from the city council, shall first apply to the
city, and in the application shall specify the property in front of which the
proposed improvement is to be made, the name of the street or streets to be
improved, the nature of the proposed improvement, and the time required for its
completion. (1996 Code § 12.04.020; amd. 2004 Code)
7-2-4: ISSUANCE OF PERMIT:
   A.   Conditions For Issuance: Permits will be issued by the city, and no
permit will be given or issued for work upon any street or any part thereof
when, or before, the design thereof has not been legally established and
accepted by the city.
   B.   Refusal Of Permit: The city may refuse a permit if in its judgment the
proposed improvement to be made is not a suitable one for the place or location
thereof, or when the improvement contemplates the removal of earth from any
street when or where it may be necessary to secure the deposit of said earth
upon any other part or parts of said street.
   C.   Contents Of Permit; Surveys For Grade: The permit provided for in this
section shall specify and provide the kind of work to be done and the time in
which same is to be completed. It shall be the duty of the applicant to make
the necessary survey and mark the grade for any improvement for which a permit
may be issued. All permits issued for the construction of cement or artificial
stone walks, sidewalks or curbs shall be accompanied by plans and
specifications therefor; and any additional information thereto deemed
pertinent by the city shall be added; and the work thereon shall be done
according to the said specifications. (1996 Code § 12.04.030; amd. 2004 Code)
7-2-5: WORK UNDER PERMIT; APPROVAL CERTIFICATE:
All work done under and in pursuance of the permit as provided in section
7-2-4 of this chapter shall be done under the supervision of the city, and upon
completion thereof shall be inspected by the city, and, if satisfactory, the
city shall issue a certificate of approval therefor, which certificate must be
countersigned by the appropriate city official, and thereafter, insofar as that
particular improvement is concerned, and as long as the same shall be in good
order and repair, the same shall be deemed a completion of that part of the
work. (1996 Code § 12.04.040; amd. 2004 Code)
7-2-6: RECORD OF PERMITS:
The city recorder shall keep accurate record of any and all permits issued
under this chapter, showing thereon the date of issuance, the person, firm or
corporation to whom issued, an accurate description of the property in front of
which the improvement is to be made, with estimate of quantity, also the date
of issuance of the certificate of approval, and in the event of the nonissuance
of the certificate of approval through reason of failure to comply with the
provisions of this chapter, the reason therefor shall be entered minutely, and
such work shall be removed whenever the city shall so direct. (1996 Code §
12.04.050; amd. 2004 Code)
7-2-7: WIDTH OF STREETS AND SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Streets: The width of streets shall be as close to compliance as is
practicable with the standards adopted by ordinance or resolution of the
council, as provided for in section
9-15-11 of this code.
   B.   Sidewalks: The width of sidewalks shall be as close to compliance as is
practicable with the standards adopted by ordinance or resolution of the
council, as provided for in section
9-15-11 of this code. (Ord. 571, 8-7-1996; amd. 2004 Code)
7-2-8: REPAIRING SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Duty To Repair:
      1.   All sidewalks in the city upon any street or alley or which are
otherwise open to the general public shall be kept in good and substantial
repair, and it shall be the duty of the owner and occupant of any premises
abutting upon the sidewalk to make such repairs and keep the same in repair.
      2.   It is unlawful for the owner and occupant of any premises to allow
any sidewalk upon or in front of the premises to be or remain out of repair, or
to be or remain out of good and substantial condition. (1996 Code § 12.04.240)
   B.   Failure To Repair; Nuisance: Any sidewalk in the city upon any street
or alley or which is otherwise open to the general public which is not kept in
good and substantial repair shall constitute a public nuisance. The owner and
occupant of the premises abutting any sidewalk which is determined to
constitute a public nuisance shall be subject to the penalty provision and
abatement procedures under title 4, chapter 1 of this code. The city shall be
allowed to proceed against the owner or occupant of the premises abutting any
sidewalk which is determined to constitute a public nuisance, without any
necessity of naming both owner and occupant. (1996 Code § 12.04.250)
CHAPTER 3
ADVANCE FINANCING OF PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS
SECTION:
7-3-1: Definitions
7-3-2: Application For Advance Financing; Fee
7-3-3: City Analysis
7-3-4: Public Hearing
7-3-5: Resolutions And Agreements
7-3-6: Advance Financed Reimbursement
7-3-7: Calculation Of Reimbursement
7-3-8: Interest Applied To Reimbursements
7-3-9: Collection Of Advance Financed Reimbursement
7-3-10: Voluntary Imposition Of Lien
7-3-11: Disposition Of Advance Financed Reimbursement
7-3-12: Recording Of Resolutions
7-3-13: Public Improvements
7-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases, for the purposes of this chapter and for the
purposes of any advance agreement entered into pursuant hereto and for any
actions taken as authorized pursuant to this chapter or otherwise, shall have
the meanings set out in this section:
ADVANCE FINANCING: A method of recapturing costs by a developer, where such
developer installs public improvements and where such public improvements may
be utilized by intervening or future properties.
ADVANCE FINANCING AGREEMENT: An agreement between developer and the city, as
authorized by the council and executed by the mayor, which provides for the
installation of and payment for advance financed public improvements and which
agreement contains improvements guarantees, provisions for reimbursement by the
intervening and future properties that may utilize such improvement, inspection
guarantees, and the like as determined in the best interest of the public by
the council.
ADVANCE FINANCING DISTRICT ORDINANCE: An ordinance adopted by the council and
executed by the mayor designating a public improvement to be an advance
financed public improvement and creating an advance financing district and
containing provisions for financial reimbursement by intervening and future
properties that may utilize the improvement and such other provisions as
determined in the best interest of the public by the council.
COUNCIL: The council of Clatskanie, Oregon.
DEVELOPER: The city, an individual, a partnership, a joint venture, a
corporation, a subdivider, a partitioner of land or any other entity, without
limitation, who will bear, under the terms of this chapter, the expense of
design, construction, purchase, installation or other expenses associated with
the creation of a public improvement. The rights of a developer, created under
the ordinance, also apply to his heirs, successors or assigns.
DEVELOPMENT: That real property being developed by the developer and for which
property the advance financing district ordinance is adopted.
FUTURE PROPERTY: That real property which may be served by the installation of
oversized or over capacity public improvements, but does not include the
development of intervening property.
INTERVENING PROPERTY: That real property abutting an advance financed public
improvement, but does not include the development of future property.
OWNER: The fee holder of record of the legal title to the real property in
question. Where such real property is being purchased under a recorded land
sales contract, then such purchasers shall also be deemed owners.
PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT: The following:
   A.   The grading, graveling, paving or other surfacing of any street, or
opening, laying out, widening, extending, altering, changing the grade of or
constructing any street.
   B.   The construction of sidewalks.
   C.   The construction or upgrading of any sanitary or storm sewer or water
main.
   D.   The construction or upgrading of any flood control dike, dam, structure
or facility.
   E.   Those "local improvements" as provided in Oregon Revised Statutes
223.387(1) as now written or hereafter amended.
   F.   Any other public improvements authorized by the council. (1996 Code §
12.06.010)
7-3-2: APPLICATION FOR ADVANCE FINANCING; FEE:
The city will receive applications for advance financing from developer, which
applications shall be submitted to the city and shall be accompanied by a fee
set by resolution. The fee will be applied for the cost of administrative
analysis of the proposed advance financing district, the cost of notifying the
property owners, recording costs and such other costs reasonably associated
with processing the application. When the city is the developer, the council
may direct the city manager to submit the application without fee. (1996 Code §
12.06.020; amd. 2004 Code)
7-3-3: CITY ANALYSIS:
Upon receipt of the advance financing application, the city shall make an
analysis of the advance financing proposal and shall prepare a report to be
submitted to the council for discussion at a public hearing. Such report shall
include a map showing the location and front footage of the development and
intervening properties, as well as the location and total acreage of all future
properties. The report shall also include an estimate of the total cost of the
advance financed public improvement. (1996 Code § 12.06.030)
7-3-4: PUBLIC HEARING:
   A.   Notification:
      1.   Not less than ten (10) nor more than thirty (30) days prior to any
public hearing being held pursuant to this chapter, developer and all
intervening and future property owners shall be notified of such hearing and
the purpose thereof. Such notification shall be accomplished by regular mail or
by personal service.
      2.   If notification is accomplished by mail, notice shall be made on the
date that said letter of notification is posted. Failure of any owner to be so
notified shall not invalidate or otherwise affect any advance financing
district ordinance or the council's action to approve or not approve the same.
(1996 Code § 12.06.040)
   B.   Conduct Of Public Hearing: After the city analysis has been completed,
an informational public hearing shall be held in which all parties and the
general public shall be given the opportunity to express their views and ask
questions pertaining to the proposed advance financed public improvement. Since
advance financed public improvements do not give rise to assessments, the
public hearing is for informational purposes only, and is not subject to
remonstrances. The council has the sole discretion after the public hearing to
decide whether or not an advance financing district ordinance shall be adopted.
(1996 Code § 12.06.050; amd. 2004 Code)
7-3-5: RESOLUTIONS AND AGREEMENTS:
After the public hearing, held pursuant to subsection
7-3-4B of this chapter, if the council desires to proceed with the advance
financed public improvement, it shall pass an advance financed district
resolution accordingly. The resolution shall designate the improvement as an
advance financial improvement and provide for advance financed reimbursement by
intervening and future property owners pursuant to this chapter. Except when
the developer is the city, the advance financing district resolution may
instruct the city to enter into an agreement between developer and the city
pertaining to the advance financed improvement, and may, in such agreement,
require such guarantee or guarantees as the city deems best to protect the
public, intervening and future properties, and may make such other provisions
as the council determines necessary and proper. (1996 Code § 12.06.060)
7-3-6: ADVANCE FINANCED REIMBURSEMENT:
An advance financed reimbursement is imposed on all intervening and future
properties for projects that utilize an advance financed public improvement
district. Such reimbursement is made at the time of utilization of the advance
financed public improvement. (1996 Code § 12.06.070)
7-3-7: CALCULATION OF REIMBURSEMENT:
   A.   Intervening Properties:
      1.   The advance financed reimbursements, imposed on intervening
properties, when future properties are not involved, shall be calculated by
dividing the total actual cost of the advance financed public improvement by
the front footage of all intervening properties which determines unit cost. The
unit cost (cost per foot) is then multiplied by the front footage of each
intervening property. In addition, the city may use any other method of
apportioning costs on those properties specially benefitted that are just and
reasonable. Interest is then applied and calculated as set out in section
7-2-8 of this chapter.
      2.   When the advance financed improvement includes future properties,
then the above calculation will be the same, except that the total cost of the
improvement shall be reduced by the cost which relates to the oversizing or
over capacity of the advance financed improvement.
      3.   In both subsections A1 and A2 of this section and subsection B of
this section, advance financing reimbursements for odd shaped lots shall be
individually established and consistent with the benefit received by the lot
and the reimbursement required of the other lots in the area. If inequities are
created through the strict implementation of the above formulas, the council
will modify its impact on a case by case basis. (1996 Code § 12.06.080)
   B.   Future Properties: The advance financed reimbursement imposed on future
properties shall be calculated by dividing the total actual cost of the advance
financed public improvement that relates to oversizing or over capacity by the
total acreage of all future properties which determines unit cost. The unit
cost (cost per acre) is then multiplied by the acreage of each future property.
In addition, the city may use any other method of apportioning costs on those
properties specially benefitted that are just and reasonable. Interest is then
applied and calculated as set out in section
7-3-8 of this chapter. (1996 Code § 12.06.090)
7-3-8: INTEREST APPLIED TO REIMBURSEMENTS:
In section
7-3-7 of this chapter, the reimbursements will be increased by interest at the
legal rate under Oregon Revised Statutes chapter 82. The interest will be
calculated from the date the council adopts the advance financing district
resolution to the date of collection of the reimbursement. (1996 Code §
12.06.100)
7-3-9: COLLECTION OF ADVANCE FINANCED REIMBURSEMENT:
   A.   Payment Due: The advance financed reimbursement is immediately due and
payable to the city by intervening or future property owners upon their
utilizing any advance financed public improvement. If connection is made or
construction commenced without the proper permits, then the advance financed
reimbursement is immediately due and payable upon the earliest date that any
such permit was required.
   B.   Permit Issuance: No permit for connection or construction shall be
issued until the advance financed reimbursement is paid in full or otherwise
processed under the terms of section
7-3-10 of this chapter. Whenever the full and correct advance financed
reimbursement has not been paid and collected for any reason, the city manager
shall report to the council the amount of the uncollected reimbursement, the
description of the real property to which the reimbursement is attributable,
the date upon which the reimbursement was due and the name or names of the
intervening or future property owners. (1996 Code § 12.06.110)
   C.   Public Hearing; Notice; Lien: The city council, by motion, shall then
set a public hearing and shall direct the city manager to give notice of that
hearing to each of those intervening and future property owners, together with
a copy of the city manager's report concerning the unpaid reimbursement, either
in person or by regular mail. Upon public hearing, the council may accept,
reject or modify the city manager's report; and if it finds that any
reimbursement is unpaid and uncollected, the council may, by motion, direct the
finance manager to record a lien on the property and said lien shall be
recorded with the county clerk. The lien shall be enforced in the manner as
provided by law. (1996 Code § 12.06.110; amd. 2004 Code)
7-3-10: VOLUNTARY IMPOSITION OF LIEN:
   A.   Application For Financing; Title Insurance:
      1.   The council may allow financing for an advance financed
reimbursement. If such option is allowed, it shall be so stated in the
resolution creating the district. If so allowed, when an advance financed
reimbursement is due and collectable, the intervening or future property owner
within the city limits may apply, upon forms provided by the city, for the
voluntary imposition of a lien upon the parcel for the full amount of the
advance financed reimbursement and the payment of that lien in twenty (20)
equal semiannual installments, including interest.
      2.   The applicant must provide a title search and, if required by the
city, a mortgagee's title insurance policy from a licensed title insurance
company showing the identity and amount of all other liens already of record
against the property and a certificate from the county tax assessor showing the
assessed valuation of the property. The city shall not permit a lien greater
than that allowed by law. Such property that lies outside the city limits must
have the permission of Columbia County in accordance with Oregon law. (1996
Code § 12.06.120)
   B.   Report Required: Upon receipt of such certificates and application, the
city shall compute the amount of the advance financed reimbursement and shall
report to the city manager the amount of the advance financed reimbursement,
the date upon which the reimbursement is due, the name or names of the
applicant/owners and the description of the property; and upon receiving that
report, the city council may, by motion, direct the city manager to record a
lien on the property and said lien shall be recorded with the county clerk.
That lien shall be enforced in the manner as provided by law. (1996 Code §
12.06.120; amd. 2004 Code)
7-3-11: DISPOSITION OF ADVANCE FINANCED REIMBURSEMENT:
   A.   Time Period For Receiving Payments: Developers shall receive the
advance financed reimbursement collected by the city for their advance financed
public improvements. Such reimbursements shall be delivered to developer for a
period of ten (10) years after execution of the advance financing agreement
unless extended by section
7-3-10 of this chapter. The time limitation does apply to the city as
developer, except for public improvements that have been advance financed prior
to the effective date hereof.
   B.   Time Limitation For Making Payments: Payments will be made to the
developer by the city within ninety (90) days of receipt of the advance
financed reimbursements, and any advance financed reimbursements not paid the
developer under the terms of this chapter shall be retained by the city to be
used for related system improvements as authorized from time to time by the
council.
   C.   Administrative Fee For City: The city shall collect an amount for
administrative services performed in collecting and distributing the
reimbursements. Such administrative fee shall reasonably reflect the service
performed and shall be set by resolution. (1996 Code § 12.06.130)
7-3-12: RECORDING OF RESOLUTIONS:
All advance finance district resolutions shall be recorded by the city in the
deed records of the county. The resolution shall contain full legal
descriptions of the development, intervening properties and future properties.
Failure to make such recording shall not affect the legality of an advance
financing resolution. (1996 Code § 12.06.140)
7-3-13: PUBLIC IMPROVEMENTS:
Public improvements installed pursuant to advance financing agreements shall
become and remain the sole property of the city pursuant to the advance
financing agreement. Advance financed reimbursements, plus interest, not paid
to the developers as set forth in section
7-3-11 of this chapter, shall be paid to the city to be used for related system
improvement as authorized from time to time by the council. (1996 Code §
12.06.150)
CHAPTER 4
PUBLIC IMPROVEMENT ASSESSMENTS
SECTION:
7-4-1: Initiation Of Proceedings And Report
7-4-2: City Council Action On Report
7-4-3: Resolution Of Intention; Notice Of Hearing
7-4-4: Manner Of Doing Work
7-4-5: Hearing; Improvement Order
7-4-6: Final Plans And Specifications
7-4-7: Call For Bids
7-4-8: Assessment Ordinance
7-4-9: Assessment Methods; Financing Alternatives
7-4-10: Remedies
7-4-11: Notice Of Assessment
7-4-12: Lien Records And Foreclosure Proceedings
7-4-13: Errors In Assessment Calculations
7-4-14: Deficit Assessment
7-4-15: Rebates
7-4-16: Abandonment Of Proceedings
7-4-17: Invalidation Of Assessment Limited
7-4-18: Reassessment
7-4-1: INITIATION OF PROCEEDINGS AND REPORT:
Whenever the city council shall deem it necessary, upon its own motion or upon
the petition of the owners of at least one-half (1/2) of the property to
benefit specially from the improvement, to make any street, sewer, sidewalk,
drain, or other public improvement to be paid for in whole or in part by
special assessment according to benefits, the city council shall, by motion,
direct an appropriate city employee or agent to make a survey and written
report for such project and file the same with the city manager. Unless the
city council directs otherwise, such report shall contain the following
matters:
   A.   A map or plat showing the general nature, location and extent of the
proposed improvement and the land to be assessed for the payment of any part of
the cost thereof.
   B.   Preliminary plans, specifications and estimates of the work to be done;
provided, however, that where the proposed project is to be carried out in
cooperation with any other governmental agency, the report may adopt the plans,
specifications and estimates of such agency.
   C.   An estimate of the probable cost of the improvement, including any
legal, administrative and engineering costs attributable thereto.
   D.   An estimate of the unit cost of the improvement to the specially
benefited properties.
   E.   A recommendation as to the method of assessment to be used to arrive at
a fair apportionment of the whole or any portion of the cost of the improvement
to the properties specially benefited.
   F.   The description and assessed value of each lot, parcel of land, or
portion thereof to be specially benefited by the improvement, with the names of
the record owners thereof and, when readily available, the names of the
contract purchasers thereof.
   G.   A statement of outstanding assessments against property to be assessed.
(1996 Code § 12.08.010)
7-4-2: CITY COUNCIL ACTION ON REPORT:
After the report shall have been filed with the city manager, the city council
may thereafter, by motion, approve the report, modify the report, and approve
it as modified; require additional or different information for such
improvement; or it may abandon the improvement. (1996 Code § 12.08.020)
7-4-3: RESOLUTION OF INTENTION; NOTICE OF HEARING:
After the city council has approved the report as submitted or modified, the
city council shall, by resolution, declare its intention to make such
improvement, provide the manner and method of carrying out the improvement, and
shall direct the city manager to give notice of such improvement by two (2)
publications one week apart in a newspaper of general circulation within the
city and by mailing copies of such notice by registered or certified mail to
the owners to be assessed for the costs of such improvement, which notice shall
contain the following matters:
   A.   That a written report on the improvement is on file in the office of
the city manager and is subject to public examination.
   B.   That the city council will hold a public hearing on the proposed
improvement on a specified date, which shall not be earlier than ten (10) days
following the first publication of notice, at which objections and
remonstrances to such improvement will be heard by the council; and that if,
prior to such hearing, there shall be presented to the city manager valid,
written remonstrances on forms provided by the city of owners of two- thirds
(2/3) of the frontage of the property to be specially affected by such
improvement, then the improvement will be abandoned for at least six (6)
months.
   C.   A description of the property to be specially benefited by the
improvement, the owners of such property, and the estimate of the unit cost of
the improvement to be specially benefited, and the total cost of the
improvement to be paid for by special assessments to benefited properties.
(1996 Code § 12.08.030)
7-4-4: MANNER OF DOING WORK:
The city council may provide in the improvement resolution that the
construction work may be done in whole or in part by the city, by a contract,
or by any other governmental agency, or by any combination thereof. (1996 Code
§ 12.08.040)
7-4-5: HEARING; IMPROVEMENT ORDER:
At the time of the public hearing on the proposed improvement, if the written
remonstrances shall represent less than the amount of property required to
defeat the proposed improvement, then, on the basis of the hearing of written
remonstrances and oral objections, if any, the city council may, by motion, at
the time of the hearing or within sixty (60) days thereafter, order the
improvement to be carried out in accordance with the resolution; or the city
council may, on its own motion, abandon the improvement. (1996 Code §
12.08.050)
7-4-6: FINAL PLANS AND SPECIFICATIONS:
The city council may, in its discretion, cause to have final plans and
specifications prepared for the proposed improvement at any time prior to the
call for bids in the event that any part of the work of the improvement is to
be done under contract bids, or at any time prior to the start of work in the
event that any part of the work is to be done by the city. (1996 Code §
12.08.060)
7-4-7: CALL FOR BIDS:
   A.   Advertisement For Bids; Bonding:
      1.   The city council may, in its discretion, direct the city manager to
advertise for bids for construction of all, or any part of, the improvement
project on the basis of the city council approved report and before the passage
of the resolution, or after the passage of the resolution and before the public
hearing on the proposed improvement, or at any time after said public hearing;
provided, however, that no contract shall be let until after the public hearing
has been held to hear remonstrances and oral objections to the proposed
improvement. In the event that any part of the work of the improvement is to be
done under contract bids, then the city council shall determine the time and
manner of advertisement for bids and the contracts may be let to the
responsible bidder whose bid is in the best interests of the city as determined
in the sole discretion of the city council; provided, that the city council
shall have the right to reject any or all bids when they are deemed
unreasonable or unsatisfactory in the city council's discretion.
      2.   The city shall provide for the bonding of all contractors for the
faithful performance of any contract let under its authority, and the
provisions thereof, in case of default, shall be enforced by action in the name
of the city.
   B.   Excessive Bid Amount; Hearing Of Objections: If the city council finds,
upon opening bids for the work of such improvement, that the bid in the best
interest of the city is substantially in excess of the estimate, it may, in its
discretion, provide for holding a special hearing of objections to the
proceeding with the improvement on the basis of such bid, and it may direct the
city manager to publish one notice thereof in a newspaper of general
circulation in the city. (1996 Code § 12.08.070)
7-4-8: ASSESSMENT ORDINANCE:
If the city council determines that the local improvement shall be made, when
the estimated cost thereof is ascertained on the basis of the contract award or
city departmental cost, or after the work is done and the cost thereof has been
actually determined, the city council shall determine whether the property
benefited shall bear all or a portion of the cost. The city manager or other
person designated by the city council shall prepare the proposed assessment to
the respective lots within the assessment district and file it in the
appropriate city office. Notice of such proposed assessment shall be mailed or
personally delivered to the owner of each lot proposed to be assessed, which
notice shall state the amounts of assessment proposed on that property and
shall fix a date by which time objections shall be filed with the city manager.
Any such objection shall state the grounds thereof. The city council shall
consider objections and may adopt, correct, modify or revise the proposed
assessments; and shall determine the amount of assessment to be charged against
each lot within the district, according to the special and peculiar benefits
accruing thereto from the improvement, and shall by ordinance spread the
assessments. (1996 Code § 12.08.080)
7-4-9: ASSESSMENT METHODS; FINANCING ALTERNATIVES:
   A.   Methods: The city council, in adopting a method of assessment of the
costs of the improvement, may:
      1.   Use any just and reasonable method of determining the extent of any
improvement district consistent with the benefits derived.
      2.   Use any method of apportioning the sum to be assessed as is just and
reasonable between the properties determined to be specially benefited.
      3.   Authorize payment by the city of all, or any part of, the cost of
any such improvement when, in the opinion of the city council, the
topographical or physical conditions, or unusual or excessive public travel, or
other character of the work involved warrants only a partial payment or no
payment by the benefited property of the costs of the improvement.
   B.   Alternatives: Nothing contained in this chapter shall preclude the city
council from using any other available means of financing improvements,
including federal or state grants in aid, sewer charges or fees, revenue bonds,
general obligation bonds, or any other legal means of finance. In the event
that such other means of financing improvements are used, the city council may,
in its discretion, levy special assessments according to the benefits derived
to cover any remaining part of the improvement. (1996 Code § 12.08.090)
7-4-10: REMEDIES:
Subject to the curative provisions of section
7-4-17 of this chapter and the rights of the city to reassess as provided in
section
7-4-18 of this chapter, proceedings for writs of review and suits in equity may
be filed no later than sixty (60) days after the passage by the city council of
the ordinance spreading the assessment; provided, that the property owner shall
have filed a written objection to the proposed assessment as provided in
section
7-4-8 of this chapter. A property owner who has filed a written objection with
the city manager, as required by section 12-4-8 of this chapter, may commence a
suit for equitable relief based on a total lack of jurisdiction on the part of
the city, and if notice of the improvement shall not have been sent to the
owner, and if the owner did not have actual knowledge of the proposed
improvement prior to the hearing, then the owner may file written objections
alleging lack of jurisdiction with the city manager within thirty (30) days
after receiving notice or knowledge of the improvement. No provision of this
section shall be construed so as to lengthen any period of redemption, or so as
to affect the running of any statute of limitation or in equitable defense of
laches. Any proceeding on a writ of review or suit in equity shall be abated if
proceedings are commenced and diligently pursued by the council to remedy or
cure the alleged errors or defects. (1996 Code § 12.08.100)
7-4-11: NOTICE OF ASSESSMENT:
Within ten (10) days after the ordinance levying has been passed, the city
manager shall send by registered or certified mail a notice of assessment to
the owner of the assessed property, and shall publish notice of such assessment
twice in a newspaper of general circulation in the city, the first publication
of which shall be made no later than ten (10) days after the date of the
assessment ordinance and shall state that, upon the failure of the owner of the
property assessed to make application to pay the assessment in installments
within ten (10) days from the date of the first publication of notice, or upon
the failure of the owner to pay the assessment in full within thirty (30) days
from the date of the assessment ordinance, then interest will commence to run
on the assessment and that the property assessed will be subject to
foreclosure, and the notice shall further set forth a description of the
property assessed, the name of the owner of the property, and the amount of
each assessment. (1996 Code § 12.08.110)
7-4-12: LIEN RECORDS AND FORECLOSURE PROCEEDINGS:
After passage of the assessment ordinance by the city council, the city manager
shall enter in the docket of city liens a statement of the amounts assessed
upon each particular lot, parcel of land, or portion thereof, together with a
description of the improvement, the name of the owners, and the date of the
assessment ordinance. Upon such entry in the lien docket, the amount so entered
shall become a lien and charge upon the respective lots, parcels of land or
portions thereof which have been assessed for such improvement. All assessment
liens of the city shall be superior and prior to all other liens or
encumbrances on property insofar as the laws of the state of Oregon permit.
Interest shall be charged at the highest rate prescribed by Oregon Revised
Statutes until paid on all amounts not paid within thirty (30) days from the
date of the assessment ordinance; and after expiration of thirty (30) days from
the date of the assessment ordinance, the city may proceed to foreclose or
enforce collection of the assessment liens in the manner provided by the
general law of the state of Oregon; provided, however, that the city may, at
its option, enter a bid for the property being offered at a foreclosure sale,
which bid shall be prior to all bids except those by persons who would be
entitled under the laws of the state to redeem such property. (1996 Code §
12.08.120; amd. 2004 Code)
7-4-13: ERRORS IN ASSESSMENT CALCULATIONS:
Claimed errors in the calculation of assessments shall be called to the
attention of the city manager, who shall determine whether there has been an
error in fact. If the city manager shall find that there has been an error in
fact, he shall recommend to the city council an amendment to the assessment
ordinance to correct such error; and upon enactment of such amendment, the city
manager shall make the necessary correction in the docket of city liens and
send a correct notice of assessment by registered or certified mail. (1996 Code
§ 12.08.130)
7-4-14: DEFICIT ASSESSMENT:
In the event that an assessment is made before the total cost of the
improvement is ascertained, and if it is found that the amount of the
assessment is insufficient to defray the expenses of the improvement, the city
council may, by motion, declare such deficit and prepare a proposed deficit
assessment. The city council shall set a time for a hearing of objections to
such deficit assessment and shall direct the city manager to publish one notice
thereof in a newspaper of general circulation in the city. After such hearing,
the city council shall make a just and equitable deficit assessment by
ordinance, which shall be entered in the docket of city liens as provided by
this chapter, and notices of the deficit assessment shall be published and
mailed, and the collection of the assessment shall be made in accordance with
sections
7-4-11 and
7-4-12 of this chapter. (1996 Code § 12.08.140)
7-4-15: REBATES:
If, upon the completion of the improvement project, it is found that the
assessment previously levied upon any property is more than sufficient to pay
the costs of such improvements, then the city council must ascertain and
declare the same by ordinance. When so declared, the excess amounts must be
entered on the lien docket as a credit upon the appropriate assessment. In the
event that any assessment has been paid, the person who paid the same, or his
legal representative, shall be entitled to the repayment of such rebate credit,
or the portion thereof which exceeds the amount unpaid on the original
assessment. (1996 Code § 12.08.150)
7-4-16: ABANDONMENT OF PROCEEDINGS:
The city council shall have full power to abandon and rescind proceedings for
improvements made under this chapter at any time prior to the final completion
of such improvements. If liens have been assessed upon any property under such
procedure, they shall be cancelled, and any payments made on such assessments
shall be refunded to the person paying the same, his assigns or legal
representatives. (1996 Code § 12.08.160)
7-4-17: INVALIDATION OF ASSESSMENT LIMITED:
No improvement assessment shall be rendered invalid by reason of a failure of
the report to contain all of the information required by section
7-4-1 of this chapter; or by reason of a failure to have all of the information
required to be in the improvement resolution, the assessment ordinance, the
lien docket, or notices required to be published and mailed; nor by the failure
to list the name of, or mail notice to, the owner of any property as required
by this chapter; or by reason of any other error, mistake, delay, omission,
irregularity, or other act, jurisdiction or otherwise, in any of the
proceedings or steps specified in this chapter, unless it appears that the
assessment is unfair or unjust in its effect upon the person complaining. The
city council shall have the power and authority to remedy and correct all such
matters by suitable actions and proceedings. (1996 Code § 12.08.170)
7-4-18: REASSESSMENT:
Whenever any assessment, deficit, or reassessment for any improvement which has
been made by the city has been, or shall be, set aside, annulled, declared or
rendered void, or its enforcement by any court of this state, or any federal
court having jurisdiction thereof, or when the city council shall be in doubt
as to the validity of such assessment, deficit assessment, or reassessment, or
any part thereof, then the city council may make a reassessment in the manner
provided by the laws of the state. (1996 Code § 12.08.180)
CHAPTER 5
STREET NAMES AND HOUSE NUMBERS
SECTION:
7-5-1: Quadrants Designated
7-5-2: Street Numbers And Names
7-5-3: Existing Street Names
7-5-4: Street Grid Map
7-5-5: Street Markers
7-5-6: House Numbering
7-5-1: QUADRANTS DESIGNATED:
The city is divided into four (4) quadrants, as follows:
U.S. Highway 30 shall be the dividing line between the north half and the south
half of the city. All areas north of said highway shall be in the north half,
and all areas south of said highway shall be in the south half of the city.
South of U.S. Highway 30, Nehalem Street shall be the dividing line between the
east and west half of the city. North of U.S. Highway 30, Nehalem Street,
running from said highway to Fifth Street shall be the dividing line between
the east and west half of the city. North of the north end of Nehalem Street,
the dividing line between the east and west half of the city shall be as
follows: A line running from the north end of Nehalem Street and in the same
direction as N. Shasta Way to its intersection with the road known as Haven
Acres Road; thence northeasterly along Haven Acres Road to its intersection
with the boundary line of the city.
(1996 Code § 12.12.010; amd. 2004 Code; Ord. 644, 3-1-2006)
7-5-2: STREET NUMBERS AND NAMES:
All numbered streets shall run in an easterly and westerly direction, and each
such street shall also be designated by the quadrant in which it is located,
such as northwest, northeast, southwest or southeast. The streets will be
numbered consecutively as they lie north or south of U.S. Highway 30. The first
street north of the highway will be known as First Street Northwest or
Northeast, as the case may be; and the first street south of the highway will
be known as First Street Southwest or Southeast, as the case may be. The second
street north of the highway will be Second Street Northwest or Northeast, as
the case may be, and the second street south of the highway will be Second
Street Southwest or Southeast, as the case may be, and so forth. The names of
the streets running in a northerly and southerly direction shall be designated
by names; and the names shall remain unchanged, unless a change is specifically
provided for by ordinance. (1996 Code § 12.12.020)
7-5-3: EXISTING STREET NAMES:
Except as specifically provided in this chapter, the names of all streets as of
the effective date hereof shall remain unchanged. (1996 Code § 12.12.030)
7-5-4: STREET GRID MAP:
   A.   Adoption: The names of all streets of the city are designated on that
certain map of the city dated January 1966. The map is by this reference
incorporated in this chapter and made a part of this chapter by this reference.
(1996 Code § 12.12.040)
   B.   Conformance Of Names And Numbers: After the effective date hereof, it
shall be the duty of the city to see that all streets conform in name and
number to the general plan indicated on the map referred to in subsection A of
this section before approving any plats and to see that any future streets or
any plats be named and numbered in accordance with the map. (1996 Code §
12.12.050; amd. 2004 Code)
7-5-5: STREET MARKERS:
All streets within the city designated by the map shall be marked. Street names
or markers shall be erected or placed at corner locations at the intersections
of all streets. The markers shall be of uniform length, breadth and letters
that will take names or numbers of the streets with the abbreviation of "St."
for streets. The cost of all markers of the streets shall be borne by the city
and shall be paid out of the general street fund. (1996 Code § 12.12.060; amd.
2004 Code)
7-5-6: HOUSE NUMBERING:
   A.   Generally:
      1.   Uniform System: A uniform system of numbering shall be furnished by
the city.
         a.   The numbers shall be one hundred (100) numbers to the block and
all numbers placed on the north and east sides of the streets shall be of even
numbers, and all numbers on the west and south sides of the streets shall be of
odd numbers.
         b.   The numbering of buildings on all named streets shall begin at
First Street with one hundred (100) and run south, and all numbering of all
numbered streets shall begin with one hundred (100) at Conyers Creek and run
west.
      2.   Cost; Supervision: The cost of numbering the buildings shall be
borne by the owners or occupants of the buildings under the supervision of the
city council. (1996 Code § 12.12.070; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Height Of Numbers: The minimum height of house numbers on residences
and business establishments in the city shall be four inches (4"). (1996 Code §
12.12.080)
CHAPTER 6
FENCES, WALLS AND HEDGES
SECTION:
7-6-1: Height Restrictions
7-6-2: Extension Beyond Property Lines
7-6-3: Attaching Signs Or Posters
7-6-4: Menacing Conditions; Thorny Hedges
7-6-5: Waiver Or Reduction Of Requirements
7-6-6: Public Nuisance Declared
7-6-7: Abatement Of Nuisances
7-6-1: HEIGHT RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Adjacent To City Streets:
      1.   Hedges, sight obscuring fences and objects within fifteen feet (15')
of the curb or edge of any city street shall not exceed a height of three feet
(3') above the established grade of the yard or of any driveway which may exist
or be constructed, whichever is lower. However, single trees on which limbs and
branches are kept removed from the tree trunk for a height of at least six feet
(6') above the established grade of the public street shall be permitted within
fifteen feet (15') of the curb or edge of any city street.
      2.   In the case of corner lots, a hedge or sight obscuring fence or
object and all flowers, shrubs and other plants may not exceed a height of two
feet (2') above the established grade for the public street within a triangular
shaped area determined by measuring a distance of thirty feet (30') from the
property corner at the street's intersection, along the property line common to
the lot and each abutting street, and the straight line necessary to connect
the above mentioned two (2) thirty foot (30') sides in order to form the third
side of the triangle; provided, that single trees, the limbs and branches of
which are kept removed from the tree trunk for a height of at least six feet
(6') above the established grade of the public street, shall be permitted.
   B.   Side Property Line: No hedge or sight obscuring fence or object on any
side property line or in the required open side yard shall be over six feet
(6') in height, except in the case of corner lots where such a hedge or fence
or object and all flowers, shrubs and other plants may not exceed a height of
two feet (2') above the grade of the public street within a triangular shaped
area determined by measuring a distance of thirty feet (30') from the property
corner at the street's intersection, along the property line common to the lot
and each abutting street and the straight line necessary to connect the above
mentioned two (2) thirty foot (30') sides in order to form the third side of
the triangle; provided, that single trees, the limbs and branches of which are
kept removed from the tree trunk for a height of at least six feet (6') above
the established grade of the public street, shall be permitted.
   C.   Rear Property Line: No hedge or sight obscuring fence on any rear
property lines, around or in any rear yard shall be over six feet (6') in
height. (1996 Code § 12.16.010)
7-6-2: EXTENSION BEYOND PROPERTY LINES:
No hedge or sight obscuring fence or object shall extend beyond the front, side
or rear property lines of any lot or plot of land 1 . (1996 Code § 12.16.020)
 
Notes
  1. See also sections
1 4-1-8 and
  9-13-2 of this code.
7-6-3: ATTACHING SIGNS OR POSTERS:
No sign or poster shall be attached in any manner to any hedge or sight
obscuring fence or object within a residential district. (1996 Code §
12.16.030)
7-6-4: MENACING CONDITIONS; THORNY HEDGES:
No hedge or sight obscuring fence or object shall be grown or maintained so as
to be a menace to life or limb of any person moving against it. Hedges of
sharp, thorny type plants shall not be permitted. (1996 Code § 12.16.040)
7-6-5: WAIVER OR REDUCTION OF REQUIREMENTS:
Recognizing that there may be situations in which the height and location of
hedges do not affect safety or the public welfare, it is hereby provided that,
notwithstanding any provision in this chapter to the contrary, where any of the
hereinafter specified conditions exist, the owner of real property may request
the city council to waive or reduce the requirements of this chapter. The city
council, upon determining that any provisions of this chapter shall be waived
or reduced for any such applicant, may impose such restrictions as they deem
necessary in view of the particular facts as represented by the owner, taking
into consideration the prevention of fires, the public health and safety, and
the surrounding neighborhood. The conditions under which the city council may
waive or reduce the requirements of this chapter are as follows:
   A.   Where the lot of the applicant is other than rectangular in shape;
   B.   Where the distance from the nearest property line of a lot to the
vehicular traveled portion of the abutting street is fifteen feet (15') or
more, and there is no pedestrian sidewalk within ten feet (10') of the property
line; or
   C.   Where unusually irregular topography exists upon the lot of the
applicant or the public street upon which the lot of the applicant abuts. (1996
Code § 12.16.050)
7-6-6: PUBLIC NUISANCE DECLARED:
All existing or new hedges or sight obscuring fences or objects grown or
constructed after the effective date hereof in violation of the provisions of
this chapter are declared to be public nuisances. (1996 Code § 12.16.070)
7-6-7: ABATEMENT OF NUISANCES:
   A.   Notice To Abate: Whenever any hedge or sight obscuring fence or object
shall have become a public nuisance, as herein defined, the city shall notify
the owner of record of the premises on which the same is located, or his agent
or person having charge or control of the premises, in writing, to remove or
abate such nuisance within thirty (30) days after receiving such notice.
   B.   Remedial Action: The person so notified shall have the right, within
the thirty (30) day period, to alter the hedge or sight obscuring fence or
object so that the same conforms to the requirements of this chapter, and if
such alteration is so made, no further action will be taken under this section.
   C.   Failure To Abate: If the person so notified shall neglect or refuse to
alter, remove or abate such nuisance, then the person so notified is in
violation of the chapter. The city manager is hereby authorized to institute in
the name of the city such proceedings as may be necessary to remedy the
nuisance and recover any city costs in any court of competent jurisdiction.
(1996 Code § 12.16.080; amd. 2004 Code)
CHAPTER 7
CAMPING
SECTION:
7-7-1: Purpose
7-7-2: Definitions
7-7-3: Camping Prohibited Upon City Property
7-7-1: PURPOSE:
This chapter is intended to balance and prioritize several interests:
recognition of the essential human dignity of everyone in the City of
Clatskanie; the need to have safe and orderly conditions in City rights-of-way
for the safety and benefit of everyone in Clatskanie; the right of everyone in
Clatskanie to have shelter for sleep and safety; and respect for public spaces
and public property in service to the entire community.
With this in mind, this chapter is intended to regulate the use of public
rights-of-way and City property to protect and preserve public places for their
designed and intended purposes, while also making them available for shelter
and sleeping by people who have no other options for shelter.
The City recognizes that surviving on City streets is typically an option of
last resort. This chapter and the City's enforcement efforts will be focused on
mitigating the impacts to public health and safety that can arise from survival
camping in public places. (Ord. 707, 6-7-2023)
7-7-2: DEFINITIONS:
For purposes of this section, the following words and phrases shall mean:
 
CAMP:              To "camp" means to occupy a campsite for over twenty- four
                   (24) hours.
CAMPSITE:          A location upon city property where camping materials are
                   placed.
                   Include, but are not limited to, tents, huts, awnings, lean-
CAMPING MATERIALS: tos, chairs, tarps, collections of personal property and/or
                   similar items that are, or reasonably appear to be, arranged
                   and/or used as camping accommodations.
 
 
                   Includes, but is not limited to, parks, rights of way,
CITY PROPERTY:     parking lots, easements, or other land owned, leased,
                   controlled, or managed by the City.
PERSONAL PROPERTY: Any item that can reasonably be identified as belonging to
                   an individual and that has apparent value or utility.
                   To move off of city property or to a different city
RELOCATE:          property. This definition does not include moving to another
                   portion of the same city property. (Ord. 707, 6-7-2023)
 
7-7-3: CAMPING PROHIBITED UPON CITY PROPERTY:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person to camp upon city property unless
otherwise authorized by law or by declaration of the City Manager.
   B.   Unless otherwise authorized by law or by declaration of the City
Manager, it is unlawful to establish a campsite and a fire for any period of
time at the following locations:
      1.   City Hall and adjacent sidewalks 75 S Nehalem Street;
      2.   Clatskanie City Park 300 Park Street;
      3.   Waste Water Treatment Plant, 100 NW 4th Street; and
      4.   City sidewalk in front of any City licensed business.
   C.   At least once every twenty-four (24) hours an individual that has
placed a campsite, camping materials or personal property on city property must
relocate.
   D.   The City shall only remove individuals and unclaimed personal property
from a campsite as provided by ORS 195.505.
   E.   Violation of this section is punishable by a fine of no more than one
hundred twenty-five dollars ($125.00). The amount imposed shall be at the
discretion of the Judge.
   F.   If the City refers a service provider to an individual who is cited for
a violation of this Section and the individual demonstrates they meaningfully
engaged with that or another similar service provider after receiving the
citation and before the hearing, the fine is eligible to be reduced or
eliminated at the discretion of the Judge. (Ord. 707, 6-7-2023)
